<h1 class="firstHeading" id="firstHeading" lang="en">New England</h1>
<div class="mw-body-content" id="bodyContent">
<div class="noprint" id="siteSub">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>
<div id="contentSub"></div>

<p><b>New England</b> is a geographical region comprising six states of the <a href="/wiki/Northeastern_United_States" title="Northeastern United States">northeastern United States</a>: <a href="/wiki/Maine" title="Maine">Maine</a>, <a href="/wiki/Vermont" title="Vermont">Vermont</a>, <a href="/wiki/New_Hampshire" title="New Hampshire">New Hampshire</a>, <a href="/wiki/Massachusetts" title="Massachusetts">Massachusetts</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rhode_Island" title="Rhode Island">Rhode Island</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Connecticut" title="Connecticut">Connecticut</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10"><a href="#cite_note-10">[a]</a></sup> It is bordered by the state of <a href="/wiki/New_York_(state)" title="New York (state)">New York</a> to the west and south, and by the <a href="/wiki/Provinces_and_territories_of_Canada" title="Provinces and territories of Canada">Canadian provinces</a> of <a href="/wiki/New_Brunswick" title="New Brunswick">New Brunswick</a> and <a href="/wiki/Quebec" title="Quebec">Quebec</a> to the northeast and north, respectively. The <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Ocean" title="Atlantic Ocean">Atlantic Ocean</a> is to the east and southeast, and <a href="/wiki/Long_Island_Sound" title="Long Island Sound">Long Island Sound</a> is to the south. <a href="/wiki/Boston" title="Boston">Boston</a>, the capital of Massachusetts, is New England's largest city. The largest metropolitan area is <a href="/wiki/Greater_Boston" title="Greater Boston">Greater Boston</a>, which also includes <a href="/wiki/Worcester,_Massachusetts" title="Worcester, Massachusetts">Worcester, Massachusetts</a> (the second-largest city in New England), <a href="/wiki/Manchester,_New_Hampshire" title="Manchester, New Hampshire">Manchester</a> (the largest city in New Hampshire), and <a href="/wiki/Providence,_Rhode_Island" title="Providence, Rhode Island">Providence</a> (the capital and largest city of <a href="/wiki/Rhode_Island" title="Rhode Island">Rhode Island</a>), with nearly a third of the entire region's population.</p>
<p>In 1620, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pilgrim_(Plymouth_Colony)" title="Pilgrim (Plymouth Colony)">Puritan Separatist Pilgrims</a> from <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_England" title="Kingdom of England">England</a> first settled in the region, forming the <a href="/wiki/Plymouth_Colony" title="Plymouth Colony">Plymouth Colony</a>, the second successful English <a href="/wiki/European_colonization_of_the_Americas" title="European colonization of the Americas">settlement</a> in the Americas, following the Jamestown Settlement in Virginia founded in 1607. Ten years later, more <a href="/wiki/Puritans" title="Puritans">Puritans</a> settled north of Plymouth Colony in Boston, thus forming <a href="/wiki/Massachusetts_Bay_Colony" title="Massachusetts Bay Colony">Massachusetts Bay Colony</a>. Over the next 126 years, people in the region fought in four <a href="/wiki/French_and_Indian_Wars" title="French and Indian Wars">French and Indian Wars</a>, until the British and their <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Iroquois_Confederacy" title="Iroquois Confederacy">Iroquois</a> allies defeated the French and their <a href="/wiki/Algonquian_peoples" title="Algonquian peoples">Algonquin</a> allies in North America. In 1692, the town of <a href="/wiki/Salem,_Massachusetts" title="Salem, Massachusetts">Salem, Massachusetts</a> and surrounding areas experienced the <a href="/wiki/Salem_witch_trials" title="Salem witch trials">Salem witch trials</a>, one of the most infamous cases of <a href="/wiki/Mass_hysteria" title="Mass hysteria">mass hysteria</a> in the history of the <a href="/wiki/Western_Hemisphere" title="Western Hemisphere">Western Hemisphere</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11"><a href="#cite_note-11">[10]</a></sup></p>
<p>In the late 18th century, political leaders from the New England Colonies known as the <a href="/wiki/Sons_of_Liberty" title="Sons of Liberty">Sons of Liberty</a> initiated resistance to Britain's efforts to impose new <a href="/wiki/No_taxation_without_representation" title="No taxation without representation">taxes without the consent of the colonists</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Boston_Tea_Party" title="Boston Tea Party">Boston Tea Party</a> was a protest to which Britain responded with a series of punitive laws stripping Massachusetts of self-government, which were termed the "<a href="/wiki/Intolerable_Acts" title="Intolerable Acts">Intolerable Acts</a>" by the colonists. The confrontation led to the first battles of the <a href="/wiki/American_Revolutionary_War" title="American Revolutionary War">American Revolutionary War</a> in 1775 and the expulsion of the British authorities from the region in spring 1776. The region also played a prominent role in the movement to <a href="/wiki/Abolitionism_in_the_United_States" title="Abolitionism in the United States">abolish slavery</a> in the United States, and was the first region of the U.S. transformed by the <a href="/wiki/Industrial_Revolution" title="Industrial Revolution">Industrial Revolution</a>, centered on the <a href="/wiki/Blackstone_Valley" title="Blackstone Valley">Blackstone</a> and <a href="/wiki/Merrimack_Valley" title="Merrimack Valley">Merrimack</a> river valleys.</p>
<p>The physical geography of New England is diverse for such a small area. Southeastern New England is covered by a narrow <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Atlantic_Coastal_Plain" title="Atlantic Coastal Plain">coastal plain</a>, while the western and northern regions are dominated by the rolling hills and worn-down peaks of the northern end of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Appalachian_Mountain" title="Appalachian Mountain">Appalachian Mountains</a>. The Atlantic <a href="/wiki/Fall_line" title="Fall line">fall line</a> lies close to the coast, which enabled numerous cities to take advantage of water power along the numerous rivers, such as the <a href="/wiki/Connecticut_River" title="Connecticut River">Connecticut River</a>, which bisects the region from north to south.</p>
<p>Each state is principally subdivided into small incorporated municipalities known as <a href="/wiki/New_England_town" title="New England town">towns</a>, many of which are governed by <a href="/wiki/Town_meeting" title="Town meeting">town meetings</a>. The only <a href="/wiki/Unincorporated_area" title="Unincorporated area">unincorporated areas</a> in the region exist in the sparsely populated northern regions of Maine, New Hampshire, and Vermont. The region is one of the U.S. Census Bureau's <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Census_Bureau_Division" title="Census Bureau Division">nine regional divisions</a> and the only multi-state region with clear, consistent boundaries. It maintains a strong sense of <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_New_England" title="Culture of New England">cultural identity</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-chiu_12-0"><a href="#cite_note-chiu-12">[11]</a></sup> although the terms of this identity are often contrasted, combining <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Puritan" title="Puritan">Puritanism</a> with liberalism, <a href="/wiki/Agrarianism" title="Agrarianism">agrarian</a> life with industry, and isolation with immigration.</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=New_England&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_New_England" title="History of New England">History of New England</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Eastern_Algonquian_peoples">Eastern Algonquian peoples</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=New_England&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Eastern Algonquian peoples">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Algonquian_peoples" title="Algonquian peoples">Algonquian peoples</a></div>
<p>The earliest known inhabitants of New England were <a href="/wiki/Indigenous_peoples_of_the_Americas" title="Indigenous peoples of the Americas">American Indians</a> who spoke a variety of the <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Algonquian_languages" title="Eastern Algonquian languages">Eastern Algonquian languages</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PVMA1_13-0"><a href="#cite_note-PVMA1-13">[12]</a></sup> Prominent tribes included the <a href="/wiki/Abenaki" title="Abenaki">Abenakis</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mi%27kmaq_people" title="Mi'kmaq people">Mi'kmaq</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Penobscot_people" title="Penobscot people">Penobscot</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pequot" title="Pequot">Pequots</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mohegans" title="Mohegans">Mohegans</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Narragansett_Indians" title="Narragansett Indians">Narragansetts</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pocumtuck" title="Pocumtuck">Pocumtucks</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Wampanoag_people" title="Wampanoag people">Wampanoag</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PVMA1_13-1"><a href="#cite_note-PVMA1-13">[12]</a></sup> Prior to the arrival of European settlers, the Western Abenakis inhabited New Hampshire, New York, and Vermont, as well as parts of <a href="/wiki/Quebec" title="Quebec">Quebec</a> and western Maine.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14"><a href="#cite_note-14">[13]</a></sup> Their principal town was <a href="/wiki/Norridgewock" title="Norridgewock">Norridgewock</a> in present-day Maine.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15"><a href="#cite_note-15">[14]</a></sup></p>
<p>The Penobscot lived along the <a href="/wiki/Penobscot_River" title="Penobscot River">Penobscot River</a> in Maine. The Narragansetts and smaller tribes under Narragansett sovereignty lived in most of modern-day Rhode Island, west of Narragansett Bay, including Block Island. The Wampanoag occupied southeastern Massachusetts, Rhode Island, and the islands of <a href="/wiki/Martha%27s_Vineyard" title="Martha's Vineyard">Martha's Vineyard</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nantucket" title="Nantucket">Nantucket</a>. The Pocumtucks lived in <a href="/wiki/Western_Massachusetts" title="Western Massachusetts">Western Massachusetts</a>, and the Mohegan and Pequot tribes lived in the Connecticut region. The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Connecticut_River_Valley" title="Connecticut River Valley">Connecticut River Valley</a> includes parts of Vermont, New Hampshire, Massachusetts, and Connecticut, linking numerous tribes culturally, linguistically, and politically.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PVMA1_13-2"><a href="#cite_note-PVMA1-13">[12]</a></sup></p>
<p>As early as 1600, <a href="/wiki/French_colonization_of_the_Americas" title="French colonization of the Americas">French</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dutch_colonization_of_the_Americas" title="Dutch colonization of the Americas">Dutch</a>, and <a href="/wiki/British_colonization_of_the_Americas" title="British colonization of the Americas">English</a> traders began exploring the <a href="/wiki/New_World" title="New World">New World</a>, trading metal, glass, and cloth for local beaver pelts.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PVMA1_13-3"><a href="#cite_note-PVMA1-13">[12]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16"><a href="#cite_note-16">[15]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Colonial_period">Colonial period</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=New_England&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Colonial period">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="The_Virginia_Companies">The Virginia Companies</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=New_England&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: The Virginia Companies">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/New_England_Colonies" title="New England Colonies">New England Colonies</a></div>
<p>On April 10, 1606, King <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/James_I_of_England" title="James I of England">James I of England</a> issued a charter for the <a href="/wiki/Virginia_Company" title="Virginia Company">Virginia Company</a>, which comprised the <a href="/wiki/London_Company" title="London Company">London Company</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Plymouth_Company" title="Plymouth Company">Plymouth Company</a>. These two privately funded ventures were intended to claim land for England, to conduct trade, and to return a profit. In 1620, Pilgrims from the <i><a href="/wiki/Mayflower" title="Mayflower">Mayflower</a></i> established <a href="/wiki/Plymouth_Colony" title="Plymouth Colony">Plymouth Colony</a> in present-day Massachusetts, beginning the history of permanent European settlement in New England.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-glocon_17-0"><a href="#cite_note-glocon-17">[16]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Plymouth_Council_for_New_England">Plymouth Council for New England</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=New_England&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Plymouth Council for New England">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Plymouth_Council_for_New_England" title="Plymouth Council for New England">Plymouth Council for New England</a>, <a href="/wiki/Connecticut_Colony" title="Connecticut Colony">Connecticut Colony</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Colony_of_Rhode_Island_and_Providence_Plantations" title="Colony of Rhode Island and Providence Plantations">Colony of Rhode Island and Providence Plantations</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Descr.of.New_England-Title_page.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="405" data-file-width="243" height="367" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/be/Descr.of.New_England-Title_page.jpg/220px-Descr.of.New_England-Title_page.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/b/be/Descr.of.New_England-Title_page.jpg 1.5x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Descr.of.New_England-Title_page.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Title page of John Smith's <i><a href="/wiki/A_Description_of_New_England" title="A Description of New England">A Description of New England</a></i> (1616)</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In 1616, English explorer <a href="/wiki/John_Smith_(explorer)" title="John Smith (explorer)">John Smith</a> named the region "New England".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18"><a href="#cite_note-18">[17]</a></sup> The name was officially sanctioned on November 3, 1620,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19"><a href="#cite_note-19">[18]</a></sup> when the charter of the Virginia Company of Plymouth was replaced by a <a href="/wiki/Royal_charter" title="Royal charter">royal charter</a> for the <a href="/wiki/Plymouth_Council_for_New_England" title="Plymouth Council for New England">Plymouth Council for New England</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Joint-stock_company" title="Joint-stock company">joint-stock company</a> established to colonize and govern the region.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20"><a href="#cite_note-20">[19]</a></sup> As the first colonists arrived in Plymouth, they wrote and signed the <a href="/wiki/Mayflower_Compact" title="Mayflower Compact">Mayflower Compact</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21"><a href="#cite_note-21">[20]</a></sup> their first governing document.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22"><a href="#cite_note-22">[21]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Massachusetts_Bay_Colony" title="Massachusetts Bay Colony">Massachusetts Bay Colony</a> came to dominate the area and was established by royal charter in 1629<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23"><a href="#cite_note-23">[22]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24"><a href="#cite_note-24">[23]</a></sup> with its major town and port of Boston established in 1630.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25"><a href="#cite_note-25">[24]</a></sup></p>
<p>Massachusetts Puritans began to settle in Connecticut as early as 1633.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26"><a href="#cite_note-26">[25]</a></sup> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Roger_Williams_(theologian)" title="Roger Williams (theologian)">Roger Williams</a> was banished from Massachusetts for heresy, led a group south, and founded <a href="/wiki/Providence_Plantations" title="Providence Plantations">Providence Plantation</a> in the area that became the <a href="/wiki/Colony_of_Rhode_Island_and_Providence_Plantations" title="Colony of Rhode Island and Providence Plantations">Colony of Rhode Island and Providence Plantations</a> in 1636.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27"><a href="#cite_note-27">[26]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28"><a href="#cite_note-28">[27]</a></sup> At this time, Vermont was yet unsettled, and the territories of <a href="/wiki/New_Hampshire" title="New Hampshire">New Hampshire</a> and <a href="/wiki/Maine" title="Maine">Maine</a> were claimed and governed by <a href="/wiki/Massachusetts" title="Massachusetts">Massachusetts</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29"><a href="#cite_note-29">[28]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="French_and_Indian_Wars">French and Indian Wars</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=New_England&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: French and Indian Wars">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Pascatway_River_New_England.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2448" data-file-width="3440" height="157" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/Pascatway_River_New_England.jpg/220px-Pascatway_River_New_England.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/Pascatway_River_New_England.jpg/330px-Pascatway_River_New_England.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/Pascatway_River_New_England.jpg/440px-Pascatway_River_New_England.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Pascatway_River_New_England.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
An early English map of New England, c. 1670, depicts the area around modern <a href="/wiki/Portsmouth,_New_Hampshire" title="Portsmouth, New Hampshire">Portsmouth, New Hampshire</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Relationships between colonists and local Indian tribes alternated between peace and armed skirmishes, the bloodiest of which was the <a href="/wiki/Pequot_War" title="Pequot War">Pequot War</a> in 1637 which resulted in the <a href="/wiki/Mystic_massacre" title="Mystic massacre">Mystic massacre</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-scw_30-0"><a href="#cite_note-scw-30">[29]</a></sup> On May 19, 1643, the colonies of <a href="/wiki/Massachusetts_Bay_Colony" title="Massachusetts Bay Colony">Massachusetts Bay</a>, <a href="/wiki/Plymouth_Colony" title="Plymouth Colony">Plymouth</a>, <a href="/wiki/New_Haven_Colony" title="New Haven Colony">New Haven</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Connecticut_Colony" title="Connecticut Colony">Connecticut</a> joined together in a loose compact called the <a href="/wiki/New_England_Confederation" title="New England Confederation">New England Confederation</a> (officially "The United Colonies of New England"). The confederation was designed largely to coordinate mutual defense, and gained some importance during <a href="/wiki/King_Philip%27s_War" title="King Philip's War">King Philip's War</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-howe_31-0"><a href="#cite_note-howe-31">[30]</a></sup> From June 1675 through April 1678, King Philip's War pitted the colonists and their Indian allies against a widespread Indian uprising, resulting in killings and massacres on both sides.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32"><a href="#cite_note-32">[31]</a></sup></p>
<p>During the next 74 years, there were six colonial wars that took place primarily between New England and <a href="/wiki/New_France" title="New France">New France</a> (see the <a href="/wiki/French_and_Indian_Wars" title="French and Indian Wars">French and Indian Wars</a> as well as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Father_Rale%27s_War" title="Father Rale's War">Father Rale's War</a> and <a href="/wiki/Father_Le_Loutre%27s_War" title="Father Le Loutre's War">Father Le Loutre's War</a>). Throughout these wars, New England was allied with the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Iroquois_Confederacy" title="Iroquois Confederacy">Iroquois Confederacy</a> and New France was allied with the <a href="/wiki/Wabanaki_Confederacy" title="Wabanaki Confederacy">Wabanaki Confederacy</a>. After the New England <a href="/wiki/Siege_of_Port_Royal_(1710)" title="Siege of Port Royal (1710)">Conquest of Acadia</a> in 1710, mainland Nova Scotia was under the control of New England, but both present-day <a href="/wiki/New_Brunswick" title="New Brunswick">New Brunswick</a> and virtually all of present-day Maine remained contested territory between New England and New France. After the British won the war in 1763, the Connecticut River Valley was opened for British settlement into western New Hampshire and what is today Vermont.</p>
<p>The New England colonies were settled primarily by farmers who became relatively self-sufficient. Later, New England's economy began to focus on crafts and trade, aided by the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Puritan_work_ethic" title="Puritan work ethic">Puritan work ethic</a>, in contrast to the Southern colonies which focused on agricultural production while importing finished goods from England.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33"><a href="#cite_note-33">[32]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Dominion_of_New_England">Dominion of New England</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=New_England&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Dominion of New England">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Dominion_of_New_England" title="Dominion of New England">Dominion of New England</a>, <a href="/wiki/American_Revolutionary_War" title="American Revolutionary War">American Revolutionary War</a>, <a href="/wiki/American_Revolution" title="American Revolution">American Revolution</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Boston_campaign" title="Boston campaign">Boston campaign</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:New_England_combo_flag.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="432" data-file-width="720" height="132" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/New_England_combo_flag.svg/220px-New_England_combo_flag.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/New_England_combo_flag.svg/330px-New_England_combo_flag.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/New_England_combo_flag.svg/440px-New_England_combo_flag.svg.png 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:New_England_combo_flag.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The New England Ensign, one of several <a href="/wiki/Flag_of_New_England" title="Flag of New England">flags historically associated with New England</a>. This flag was reportedly used by colonial merchant ships sailing out of New England ports, 1686 – c. 1737.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-David_B._Martucci_34-0"><a href="#cite_note-David_B._Martucci-34">[33]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35"><a href="#cite_note-35">[34]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36"><a href="#cite_note-36">[35]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37"><a href="#cite_note-37">[36]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38"><a href="#cite_note-38">[37]</a></sup></div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Louisbourg_assiegee_en_1745.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="617" data-file-width="1200" height="113" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/28/Louisbourg_assiegee_en_1745.jpg/220px-Louisbourg_assiegee_en_1745.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/28/Louisbourg_assiegee_en_1745.jpg/330px-Louisbourg_assiegee_en_1745.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/28/Louisbourg_assiegee_en_1745.jpg/440px-Louisbourg_assiegee_en_1745.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Louisbourg_assiegee_en_1745.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
New England's <i><a href="/wiki/Siege_of_Louisbourg_(1745)" title="Siege of Louisbourg (1745)">Siege of Louisbourg</a></i> (1745) by <a href="/wiki/Peter_Monamy" title="Peter Monamy">Peter Monamy</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>By 1686, <a href="/wiki/James_II_of_England" title="James II of England">King James II</a> had become concerned about the increasingly independent ways of the colonies, including their self-governing charters, their open flouting of the <a href="/wiki/Navigation_Acts" title="Navigation Acts">Navigation Acts</a>, and their growing military power. He therefore established the <a href="/wiki/Dominion_of_New_England" title="Dominion of New England">Dominion of New England</a>, an administrative union comprising all of the New England colonies.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CTHeritage_39-0"><a href="#cite_note-CTHeritage-39">[38]</a></sup> In 1688, the former Dutch colonies of <a href="/wiki/Province_of_New_York" title="Province of New York">New York</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/East_New_Jersey" title="East New Jersey">East New Jersey</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/West_New_Jersey" title="West New Jersey">West New Jersey</a> were added to the Dominion. The union was imposed from the outside and contrary to the rooted democratic tradition of the region, and it was highly unpopular among the colonists.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Palfrey_40-0"><a href="#cite_note-Palfrey-40">[39]</a></sup></p>
<p>The Dominion significantly modified the charters of the colonies, including the appointment of Royal Governors to nearly all of them. There was an uneasy tension between the Royal Governors, their officers, and the elected governing bodies of the colonies. The governors wanted unlimited authority, and the different layers of locally elected officials would often resist them. In most cases, the local town governments continued operating as self-governing bodies, just as they had before the appointment of the governors.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41"><a href="#cite_note-41">[40]</a></sup></p>
<p>After the <a href="/wiki/Glorious_Revolution" title="Glorious Revolution">Glorious Revolution</a> in 1689, Bostonians overthrew royal governor <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sir_Edmund_Andros" title="Sir Edmund Andros">Sir Edmund Andros</a>. They seized dominion officials and adherents to the <a href="/wiki/Church_of_England" title="Church of England">Church of England</a> during a <a href="/wiki/1689_Boston_revolt" title="1689 Boston revolt">popular and bloodless uprising</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42"><a href="#cite_note-42">[41]</a></sup> These tensions eventually culminated in the <a href="/wiki/American_Revolution" title="American Revolution">American Revolution</a>, boiling over with the outbreak of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/War_of_American_Independence" title="War of American Independence">War of American Independence</a> in 1775. The first battles of the war were fought in <a href="/wiki/Battles_of_Lexington_and_Concord" title="Battles of Lexington and Concord">Lexington and Concord, Massachusetts</a>, later leading to the <a href="/wiki/Siege_of_Boston" title="Siege of Boston">Siege of Boston</a> by continental troops. In March 1776, British forces were compelled to retreat from Boston.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="New_England_in_the_new_nation">New England in the new nation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=New_England&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: New England in the new nation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:BCburnslawnsunset.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="816" data-file-width="1203" height="149" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8e/BCburnslawnsunset.jpg/220px-BCburnslawnsunset.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8e/BCburnslawnsunset.jpg/330px-BCburnslawnsunset.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8e/BCburnslawnsunset.jpg/440px-BCburnslawnsunset.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:BCburnslawnsunset.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Boston_College" title="Boston College">Boston College</a>: the architecture style is <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Collegiate_Gothic_in_North_America" title="Collegiate Gothic in North America">Collegiate Gothic</a>, a subgenre of <a href="/wiki/Gothic_Revival_architecture" title="Gothic Revival architecture">Gothic Revival architecture</a>, a 19th-century movement.</div>
</div>
</div>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Post-Revolutionary_New_England">Post-Revolutionary New England</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=New_England&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Post-Revolutionary New England">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>After the dissolution of the Dominion of New England, the colonies of New England ceased to function as a unified political unit but remained a defined cultural region. By 1784, all of the states in the region had taken steps towards the abolition of slavery, with Vermont and Massachusetts introducing total abolition in 1777 and 1783, respectively.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43"><a href="#cite_note-43">[42]</a></sup> The nickname "Yankeeland" was sometimes used to denote the New England area, especially among Southerners and British.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44"><a href="#cite_note-44">[43]</a></sup></p>
<p>After settling a dispute with New York, Vermont was admitted to statehood in 1791, formally completing the defined area of New England. On March 15, 1820, as part of the <a href="/wiki/Missouri_Compromise" title="Missouri Compromise">Missouri Compromise</a>, the territory of Maine, formerly a part of Massachusetts, was admitted to the <a href="/wiki/Union_(American_Civil_War)" title="Union (American Civil War)">Union</a> as a free state.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45"><a href="#cite_note-45">[44]</a></sup> Today, New England is defined as the six states of Connecticut, Maine, Massachusetts, New Hampshire, Rhode Island, and Vermont.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Britannica_5-1"><a href="#cite_note-Britannica-5">[5]</a></sup></p>
<p>For the rest of the period before the <a href="/wiki/American_Civil_War" title="American Civil War">American Civil War</a>, New England remained distinct from the rest of the United States. New England's economic growth relied heavily on trade with the <a href="/wiki/British_Empire" title="British Empire">British Empire</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46"><a href="#cite_note-46">[45]</a></sup> and the region's merchants and politicians strongly opposed trade restrictions. As the United States and the United Kingdom fought the <a href="/wiki/War_of_1812" title="War of 1812">War of 1812</a>, New England <a href="/wiki/Federalist_Party" title="Federalist Party">Federalists</a> organized the <a href="/wiki/Hartford_Convention" title="Hartford Convention">Hartford Convention</a> in the winter of 1814 to discuss the region's grievances concerning the war, and to propose changes to the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Constitution" title="United States Constitution">Constitution</a> to protect the region's interests and maintain its political power.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47"><a href="#cite_note-47">[46]</a></sup> Radical delegates within the convention proposed the region's <a href="/wiki/Secession_in_the_United_States" title="Secession in the United States">secession</a> from the United States, but they were outnumbered by moderates who opposed the idea.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48"><a href="#cite_note-48">[47]</a></sup></p>
<p>Politically, the region often disagreed with the rest of the country.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49"><a href="#cite_note-49">[48]</a></sup> Massachusetts and Connecticut were among the last refuges of the <a href="/wiki/Federalist_Party" title="Federalist Party">Federalist Party</a>, and New England became the strongest bastion of the new <a href="/wiki/Whig_Party_(United_States)" title="Whig Party (United States)">Whig Party</a> when the <a href="/wiki/Second_Party_System" title="Second Party System">Second Party System</a> began in the 1830s. The Whigs were usually dominant throughout New England, except in the more <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Party_(United_States)" title="Democratic Party (United States)">Democratic</a> Maine and New Hampshire. Leading statesmen hailed from the region, including <a href="/wiki/Daniel_Webster" title="Daniel Webster">Daniel Webster</a>.</p>
<p>New England was distinct in other ways, as well. Many notable literary and intellectual figures were New Englanders, produced by the United States before the American Civil War, including <a href="/wiki/Ralph_Waldo_Emerson" title="Ralph Waldo Emerson">Ralph Waldo Emerson</a>, <a href="/wiki/Henry_David_Thoreau" title="Henry David Thoreau">Henry David Thoreau</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nathaniel_Hawthorne" title="Nathaniel Hawthorne">Nathaniel Hawthorne</a>, <a href="/wiki/Henry_Wadsworth_Longfellow" title="Henry Wadsworth Longfellow">Henry Wadsworth Longfellow</a>, <a href="/wiki/John_Greenleaf_Whittier" title="John Greenleaf Whittier">John Greenleaf Whittier</a>, <a href="/wiki/George_Bancroft" title="George Bancroft">George Bancroft</a>, and <a href="/wiki/William_H._Prescott" title="William H. Prescott">William H. Prescott</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50"><a href="#cite_note-50">[49]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Industrial_Revolution">Industrial Revolution</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=New_England&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Industrial Revolution">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Pawtucket_slater_mill.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2048" data-file-width="1536" height="293" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Pawtucket_slater_mill.jpg/220px-Pawtucket_slater_mill.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Pawtucket_slater_mill.jpg/330px-Pawtucket_slater_mill.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Pawtucket_slater_mill.jpg/440px-Pawtucket_slater_mill.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Pawtucket_slater_mill.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The <a href="/wiki/Slater_Mill_Historic_Site" title="Slater Mill Historic Site">Slater Mill Historic Site</a> in <a href="/wiki/Pawtucket,_Rhode_Island" title="Pawtucket, Rhode Island">Pawtucket, Rhode Island</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>New England was key to the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Industrial_revolution" title="Industrial revolution">industrial revolution</a> in the United States.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-encarta_51-0"><a href="#cite_note-encarta-51">[50]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Blackstone_Valley" title="Blackstone Valley">Blackstone Valley</a> running through Massachusetts and Rhode Island has been called the birthplace of America's industrial revolution.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52"><a href="#cite_note-52">[51]</a></sup> In 1787, the first cotton mill in America was founded in the <a href="/wiki/North_Shore_(Massachusetts)" title="North Shore (Massachusetts)">North Shore</a> seaport of <a href="/wiki/Beverly,_Massachusetts" title="Beverly, Massachusetts">Beverly, Massachusetts</a> as the <a href="/wiki/Beverly_Cotton_Manufactory" title="Beverly Cotton Manufactory">Beverly Cotton Manufactory</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53"><a href="#cite_note-53">[52]</a></sup> The Manufactory was also considered the largest cotton mill of its time. Technological developments and achievements from the Manufactory led to the development of more advanced cotton mills, including <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Slater_Mill" title="Slater Mill">Slater Mill</a> in <a href="/wiki/Pawtucket,_Rhode_Island" title="Pawtucket, Rhode Island">Pawtucket, Rhode Island</a>. Towns such as <a href="/wiki/Lawrence,_Massachusetts" title="Lawrence, Massachusetts">Lawrence, Massachusetts</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lowell,_Massachusetts" title="Lowell, Massachusetts">Lowell, Massachusetts</a>, <a href="/wiki/Woonsocket,_Rhode_Island" title="Woonsocket, Rhode Island">Woonsocket, Rhode Island</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Lewiston,_Maine" title="Lewiston, Maine">Lewiston, Maine</a> became centers of the textile industry following the innovations at Slater Mill and the Beverly Cotton Manufactory.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Connecticut_River_Valley" title="Connecticut River Valley">Connecticut River Valley</a> became a crucible for industrial innovation, particularly the <a href="/wiki/Springfield_Armory" title="Springfield Armory">Springfield Armory</a>, pioneering such advances as <a href="/wiki/Interchangeable_parts" title="Interchangeable parts">interchangeable parts</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Assembly_line" title="Assembly line">assembly line</a> which influenced manufacturing processes all around the world.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54"><a href="#cite_note-54">[53]</a></sup> From early in the nineteenth century until the mid-twentieth, the region surrounding <a href="/wiki/Springfield,_Massachusetts" title="Springfield, Massachusetts">Springfield, Massachusetts</a> and <a href="/wiki/Hartford,_Connecticut" title="Hartford, Connecticut">Hartford, Connecticut</a> served as the United States' epicenter for <a href="/wiki/Advanced_manufacturing" title="Advanced manufacturing">advanced manufacturing</a>, drawing skilled workers from all over the world.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55"><a href="#cite_note-55">[54]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56"><a href="#cite_note-56">[55]</a></sup></p>
<p>The rapid growth of textile manufacturing in New England between 1815 and 1860 caused a shortage of workers. Recruiters were hired by mill agents to bring young women and children from the countryside to work in the factories. Between 1830 and 1860, thousands of farm girls moved from rural areas where there was no paid employment to work in the nearby mills, such as the famous <a href="/wiki/Lowell_Mill_Girls" title="Lowell Mill Girls">Lowell Mill Girls</a>. As the textile industry grew, immigration also grew. By the 1850s, immigrants began working in the mills, especially <a href="/wiki/Irish_Americans" title="Irish Americans">Irish</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/French_American" title="French American">French Canadians</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57"><a href="#cite_note-57">[56]</a></sup></p>
<p>New England as a whole was the most industrialized part of the U.S. By 1850, the region accounted for well over a quarter of all manufacturing value in the country and over a third of its industrial workforce.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1850_census_58-0"><a href="#cite_note-1850_census-58">[57]</a></sup> It was also the most literate and most educated region in the country.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1850_census_58-1"><a href="#cite_note-1850_census-58">[57]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Anti-slavery">Anti-slavery</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=New_England&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Anti-slavery">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>During the same period, New England and areas settled by New Englanders (upstate New York, Ohio's <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Western_Reserve" title="Western Reserve">Western Reserve</a>, and the upper midwestern states of <a href="/wiki/Michigan" title="Michigan">Michigan</a> and <a href="/wiki/Wisconsin" title="Wisconsin">Wisconsin</a>) were the center of the strongest abolitionist and anti-slavery movements in the United States, coinciding with the Protestant <a href="/wiki/Great_Awakening" title="Great Awakening">Great Awakening</a> in the region.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-wyattbrown_59-0"><a href="#cite_note-wyattbrown-59">[58]</a></sup> Abolitionists who demanded immediate emancipation such as <a href="/wiki/William_Lloyd_Garrison" title="William Lloyd Garrison">William Lloyd Garrison</a>, <a href="/wiki/John_Greenleaf_Whittier" title="John Greenleaf Whittier">John Greenleaf Whittier</a> and <a href="/wiki/Wendell_Phillips" title="Wendell Phillips">Wendell Phillips</a> had their base in the region. So too did anti-slavery politicians who wanted to limit the growth of slavery, such as <a href="/wiki/John_Quincy_Adams" title="John Quincy Adams">John Quincy Adams</a>, <a href="/wiki/Charles_Sumner" title="Charles Sumner">Charles Sumner</a>, and <a href="/wiki/John_P._Hale" title="John P. Hale">John P. Hale</a>. When the anti-slavery <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/History_of_the_Republican_Party_(United_States)" title="History of the Republican Party (United States)">Republican Party</a> was formed in the 1850s, all of New England, including areas that had previously been strongholds for both the Whig and the Democratic Parties, became strongly Republican. New England remained solidly Republican until Catholics began to mobilize behind the Democrats, especially in 1928, and up until the Republican party realigned its politics in a shift known as the <a href="/wiki/Southern_strategy" title="Southern strategy">Southern strategy</a>. This led to the end of "Yankee Republicanism" and began New England's relatively swift transition into a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Blue_wall_(electoral_college)" title="Blue wall (electoral college)">consistently Democratic stronghold</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tarr_60-0"><a href="#cite_note-tarr-60">[59]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="20th_century_and_beyond">20th century and beyond</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=New_England&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: 20th century and beyond">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Autumn_in_New_England_Maurice_Prendergast.jpeg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="678" data-file-width="931" height="160" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/Autumn_in_New_England_Maurice_Prendergast.jpeg/220px-Autumn_in_New_England_Maurice_Prendergast.jpeg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/Autumn_in_New_England_Maurice_Prendergast.jpeg/330px-Autumn_in_New_England_Maurice_Prendergast.jpeg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/Autumn_in_New_England_Maurice_Prendergast.jpeg/440px-Autumn_in_New_England_Maurice_Prendergast.jpeg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Autumn_in_New_England_Maurice_Prendergast.jpeg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<i>Autumn in New England</i>, watercolor, <a href="/wiki/Maurice_Prendergast" title="Maurice Prendergast">Maurice Prendergast</a>. C. 1910–1913</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The flow of immigrants continued at a steady pace from the 1840s until cut off by <a href="/wiki/World_War_I" title="World War I">World War I</a>. The largest numbers came from Ireland and Britain before 1890, and after that from Quebec, Italy and Southern Europe. The immigrants filled the ranks of factory workers, craftsmen and unskilled laborers. The Irish assumed a larger and larger role in the Democratic Parts in the cities and statewide, while the rural areas remained Republican. Yankees left the farms, which never were highly productive; many headed west, while others became professionals and businessmen in the New England cities.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Great_Depression">Great Depression</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=New_England&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Great Depression">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Great_Depression_in_the_United_States" title="Great Depression in the United States">Great Depression in the United States</a> of the 1930s hit the region hard, with high unemployment in the industrial cities. The Democrats appealed to factory workers and especially Catholics, pulling them into the <a href="/wiki/New_Deal_coalition" title="New Deal coalition">New Deal coalition</a> and making the once-Republican region into one that was closely divided. However the enormous spending on munitions, ships, electronics, and uniforms during <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a> caused a burst of prosperity in every sector.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Deindustrialization">Deindustrialization</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=New_England&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Deindustrialization">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:NewEngland_Fall.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2111" data-file-width="3363" height="138" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/NewEngland_Fall.jpg/220px-NewEngland_Fall.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/NewEngland_Fall.jpg/330px-NewEngland_Fall.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/NewEngland_Fall.jpg/440px-NewEngland_Fall.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:NewEngland_Fall.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Autumn_leaf_color" title="Autumn leaf color">Fall foliage</a> in the town of <a href="/wiki/Stowe,_Vermont" title="Stowe, Vermont">Stowe, Vermont</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The region lost most of its factories starting with the loss of textiles in the 1930s and getting worse after 1960. The New England economy was radically transformed after World War II. The factory economy practically disappeared. Like urban centers in the <a href="/wiki/Rust_Belt" title="Rust Belt">Rust Belt</a>, once-bustling New England communities fell into economic decay following the flight of the region's industrial base. The textile mills one by one went out of business from the 1920s to the 1970s. For example, the Crompton Company, after 178 years in business, went bankrupt in 1984, costing the jobs of 2,450 workers in five states. The major reasons were cheap imports, the strong dollar, declining exports, and a failure to diversify.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61"><a href="#cite_note-61">[60]</a></sup> Shoes followed.</p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:AlexanderKingHouseSuffieldCT.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="561" data-file-width="750" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/AlexanderKingHouseSuffieldCT.jpg/220px-AlexanderKingHouseSuffieldCT.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/AlexanderKingHouseSuffieldCT.jpg/330px-AlexanderKingHouseSuffieldCT.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/AlexanderKingHouseSuffieldCT.jpg/440px-AlexanderKingHouseSuffieldCT.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:AlexanderKingHouseSuffieldCT.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Alexander King House in <a href="/wiki/Suffield,_Connecticut" title="Suffield, Connecticut">Suffield, Connecticut</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>What remains is very high technology manufacturing, such as jet engines, nuclear submarines, pharmaceuticals, robotics, scientific instruments, and medical devices. MIT (the Massachusetts Institute of Technology) invented the format for university-industry relations in high tech fields, and spawned many software and hardware firms, some of which grew rapidly.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62"><a href="#cite_note-62">[61]</a></sup> By the 21st century the region had become famous for its leadership roles in the fields of education, medicine and medical research, high-technology, finance, and tourism.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63"><a href="#cite_note-63">[62]</a></sup></p>
<p>Some industrial areas were slow in adjusting to the new service economy. In 2000, New England had two of the ten poorest cities (by percentage living below the poverty line) in the U.S.: the state capitals of <a href="/wiki/Providence,_Rhode_Island" title="Providence, Rhode Island">Providence, Rhode Island</a> and <a href="/wiki/Hartford,_Connecticut" title="Hartford, Connecticut">Hartford, Connecticut</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64"><a href="#cite_note-64">[63]</a></sup> They were no longer in the bottom ten by 2010; Connecticut, Massachusetts, and New Hampshire remain among the ten wealthiest states in the United States in terms of median household income and per capita income.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65"><a href="#cite_note-65">[64]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Cities_and_urban_areas">Cities and urban areas</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=New_England&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Cities and urban areas">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=New_England&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Geography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Geography_of_Connecticut" title="Geography of Connecticut">Geography of Connecticut</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Geography_of_Maine" title="Geography of Maine">Geography of Maine</a>, <a href="/wiki/Geography_of_Massachusetts" title="Geography of Massachusetts">Geography of Massachusetts</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Geography_of_New_Hampshire" title="Geography of New Hampshire">Geography of New Hampshire</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Geography_of_Rhode_Island" title="Geography of Rhode Island">Geography of Rhode Island</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Geography_of_Vermont" title="Geography of Vermont">Geography of Vermont</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:New_england_ref_2001.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1361" data-file-width="900" height="378" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7f/New_england_ref_2001.jpg/250px-New_england_ref_2001.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7f/New_england_ref_2001.jpg/375px-New_england_ref_2001.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7f/New_england_ref_2001.jpg/500px-New_england_ref_2001.jpg 2x" width="250"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:New_england_ref_2001.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
A political and geographical map of New England shows the <a href="/wiki/Coastal_plain" title="Coastal plain">coastal plains</a> in the east, and hills, mountains and valleys in the west and the north.</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Pioneer_Valley_South_From_Mt._Sugarloaf.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1704" data-file-width="2272" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c0/Pioneer_Valley_South_From_Mt._Sugarloaf.jpg/220px-Pioneer_Valley_South_From_Mt._Sugarloaf.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c0/Pioneer_Valley_South_From_Mt._Sugarloaf.jpg/330px-Pioneer_Valley_South_From_Mt._Sugarloaf.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c0/Pioneer_Valley_South_From_Mt._Sugarloaf.jpg/440px-Pioneer_Valley_South_From_Mt._Sugarloaf.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Pioneer_Valley_South_From_Mt._Sugarloaf.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
A portion of the north-central <a href="/wiki/Pioneer_Valley" title="Pioneer Valley">Pioneer Valley</a> in <a href="/wiki/Sunderland,_Massachusetts" title="Sunderland, Massachusetts">Sunderland, Massachusetts</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The states of New England have a combined area of 71,991.8 square miles (186,458 km<sup>2</sup>), making the region slightly larger than the <a href="/wiki/Washington_(state)" title="Washington (state)">state of Washington</a> and larger than England.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66"><a href="#cite_note-66">[65]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67"><a href="#cite_note-67">[66]</a></sup> Maine alone constitutes nearly one-half of the total area of New England, yet is only the 39th-largest state, slightly smaller than <a href="/wiki/Indiana" title="Indiana">Indiana</a>. The remaining states are among the smallest in the U.S., including the <a href="/wiki/List_of_U.S._states_and_territories_by_area" title="List of U.S. states and territories by area">smallest state</a>, Rhode Island.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Geology">Geology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=New_England&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Geology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Geology_of_New_England" title="Geology of New England">Geology of New England</a></div>
<p>New England's long rolling hills, mountains, and jagged coastline are <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Glacial_landforms" title="Glacial landforms">glacial landforms</a> resulting from the retreat of ice sheets approximately 18,000 years ago, during the <a href="/wiki/Last_glacial_period" title="Last glacial period">last glacial period</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PRI-4_68-0"><a href="#cite_note-PRI-4-68">[67]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EmersonP_69-0"><a href="#cite_note-EmersonP-69">[68]</a></sup></p>
<p>New England is geologically a part of the <a href="/wiki/New_England_province" title="New England province">New England province</a>, an <a href="/wiki/Terrane" title="Terrane">exotic terrane</a> region consisting of the <a href="/wiki/Appalachian_Mountains" title="Appalachian Mountains">Appalachian Mountains</a>, the New England highlands, and the seaboard lowlands.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-USGS-Water_70-0"><a href="#cite_note-USGS-Water-70">[69]</a></sup> The Appalachian Mountains roughly follow the border between New England and New York. <a href="/wiki/The_Berkshires" title="The Berkshires">The Berkshires</a> in Massachusetts and Connecticut, and the <a href="/wiki/Green_Mountains" title="Green Mountains">Green Mountains</a> in Vermont, as well as the <a href="/wiki/Taconic_Mountains" title="Taconic Mountains">Taconic Mountains</a>, form a spine of <a href="/wiki/Precambrian" title="Precambrian">Precambrian</a> rock.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PRI-2_71-0"><a href="#cite_note-PRI-2-71">[70]</a></sup></p>
<p>The Appalachians extend northwards into New Hampshire as the <a href="/wiki/White_Mountains_(New_Hampshire)" title="White Mountains (New Hampshire)">White Mountains</a>, and then into Maine and Canada. <a href="/wiki/Mount_Washington_(New_Hampshire)" title="Mount Washington (New Hampshire)">Mount Washington</a> in New Hampshire is the highest peak in the Northeast, although it is not among the ten highest peaks in the eastern United States.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72"><a href="#cite_note-72">[71]</a></sup> It is the site of the second <a href="/wiki/Wind_speed#Highest_speed" title="Wind speed">highest recorded wind speed</a> on Earth,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73"><a href="#cite_note-73">[72]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74"><a href="#cite_note-74">[73]</a></sup> and has the reputation of having the world's most severe weather.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MWOBS_75-0"><a href="#cite_note-MWOBS-75">[74]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76"><a href="#cite_note-76">[75]</a></sup></p>
<p>The coast of the region, extending from southwestern Connecticut to northeastern Maine, is dotted with lakes, hills, marshes and wetlands, and sandy beaches.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EmersonP_69-1"><a href="#cite_note-EmersonP-69">[68]</a></sup> Important valleys in the region include the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Connecticut_River_Valley" title="Connecticut River Valley">Connecticut River Valley</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Merrimack_Valley" title="Merrimack Valley">Merrimack Valley</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EmersonP_69-2"><a href="#cite_note-EmersonP-69">[68]</a></sup> The longest river is the <a href="/wiki/Connecticut_River" title="Connecticut River">Connecticut River</a>, which flows from northeastern New Hampshire for 655 km (407 mi), emptying into <a href="/wiki/Long_Island_Sound" title="Long Island Sound">Long Island Sound</a>, roughly bisecting the region. <a href="/wiki/Lake_Champlain" title="Lake Champlain">Lake Champlain</a>, wedged between Vermont and New York, is the largest lake in the region, followed by <a href="/wiki/Moosehead_Lake" title="Moosehead Lake">Moosehead Lake</a> in Maine and <a href="/wiki/Lake_Winnipesaukee" title="Lake Winnipesaukee">Lake Winnipesaukee</a> in New Hampshire.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EmersonP_69-3"><a href="#cite_note-EmersonP-69">[68]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">Climate</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=New_England&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Climate">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Climate_of_New_England" title="Climate of New England">Climate of New England</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:NewEngland_koeppen.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="9900" data-file-width="6000" height="363" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/95/NewEngland_koeppen.png/220px-NewEngland_koeppen.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/95/NewEngland_koeppen.png/330px-NewEngland_koeppen.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/95/NewEngland_koeppen.png/440px-NewEngland_koeppen.png 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:NewEngland_koeppen.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification" title="Köppen climate classification">Köppen climate types</a> in New England</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:FranconiaRidgeTrail.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="289" data-file-width="432" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/15/FranconiaRidgeTrail.jpg/220px-FranconiaRidgeTrail.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/15/FranconiaRidgeTrail.jpg/330px-FranconiaRidgeTrail.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/1/15/FranconiaRidgeTrail.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:FranconiaRidgeTrail.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The <a href="/wiki/White_Mountains_(New_Hampshire)" title="White Mountains (New Hampshire)">White Mountains</a> of New Hampshire are part of the <a href="/wiki/Appalachian_Mountains" title="Appalachian Mountains">Appalachian Mountains</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The climate of New England varies greatly across its 500 miles (800 km) span from northern Maine to southern Connecticut:</p>
<p>Maine, northern and central New Hampshire, Vermont, and western Massachusetts have a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Humid_continental" title="Humid continental">humid continental</a> climate (Dfb in <a href="/wiki/K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification" title="Köppen climate classification">Köppen climate classification</a>). In this region the winters are long, cold, and heavy snow is common (most locations receive 60 to 120 inches (1,500 to 3,000 mm) of snow annually in this region). The summer's months are moderately warm, though summer is rather short and rainfall is spread through the year.</p>
<p>In central and eastern Massachusetts, southeastern New Hampshire, Rhode Island, and most of Connecticut, the same humid continental prevails (Dfa), though summers are warm to hot, winters are shorter, and there is less snowfall (especially in the coastal areas where it is often warmer).</p>
<p>Southern and coastal Connecticut is the broad transition zone from the cold continental climates of the north to the milder temperate/subtropical climates to the south. The frost free season is greater than 180 days across far southern/coastal Connecticut, coastal Rhode Island, and the islands (Nantucket and Martha's Vineyard). Winters also tend to be much sunnier in southern Connecticut and southern Rhode Island compared to the rest of New England.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77"><a href="#cite_note-77">[76]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=New_England&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Demographics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Demographics_of_New_England" title="Demographics of New England">Demographics of New England</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:New_England_ancestry_by_county_-_updated.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1234" data-file-width="1481" height="183" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5f/New_England_ancestry_by_county_-_updated.png/220px-New_England_ancestry_by_county_-_updated.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5f/New_England_ancestry_by_county_-_updated.png/330px-New_England_ancestry_by_county_-_updated.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5f/New_England_ancestry_by_county_-_updated.png/440px-New_England_ancestry_by_county_-_updated.png 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:New_England_ancestry_by_county_-_updated.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Largest self-reported ancestry groups in New England. Americans of Irish descent form a plurality in most of Massachusetts, and Americans of English descent form a plurality in much of the central parts of Vermont and New Hampshire as well as nearly all of Maine.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In 2010, New England had a population of 14,444,865, a growth of 3.8% from 2000.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-RIcensus_78-0"><a href="#cite_note-RIcensus-78">[77]</a></sup> This grew to an estimated 14,727,584 by 2015.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79"><a href="#cite_note-79">[78]</a></sup> Massachusetts is the most populous state with 6,794,422 residents, while Vermont is the least populous state with 626,042 residents.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-RIcensus_78-1"><a href="#cite_note-RIcensus-78">[77]</a></sup> Boston is by far the region's most populous city and metropolitan area.</p>
<p>Although a great disparity exists between New England's northern and southern portions, the region's average population density is 234.93 inhabitants/sq mi (90.7/km²). New England has a significantly higher population density than that of the U.S. as a whole (79.56/sq mi), or even just the contiguous 48 states (94.48/sq mi). Three-quarters of the population of New England, and most of the major cities, are in the states of Connecticut, Massachusetts, and Rhode Island. The combined population density of these states is 786.83/sq mi, compared to northern New England's 63.56/sq mi (2000 census).</p>
<p>According to the 2006–08 <a href="/wiki/American_Community_Survey" title="American Community Survey">American Community Survey</a>, 48.7% of New Englanders were male and 51.3% were female. Approximately 22.4% of the population were under 18 years of age; 13.5% were over 65 years of age. The six states of New England have the lowest birth rate in the U.S.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80"><a href="#cite_note-80">[79]</a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/White_Americans" title="White Americans">White Americans</a> make up the majority of New England's population at 83.4% of the total population, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hispanic_and_Latino_American" title="Hispanic and Latino American">Hispanic and Latino Americans</a> are New England's largest minority, and they are the second-largest group in the region behind non-Hispanic <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/European_American" title="European American">European Americans</a>. As of 2014, Hispanics and Latinos of any race made up 10.2% of New England's population. Connecticut had the highest proportion at 13.9%, while Vermont had the lowest at 1.3%. There were nearly 1.5 million Hispanic and Latino individuals reported in New England in 2014. <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Ricans_in_the_United_States" title="Puerto Ricans in the United States">Puerto Ricans</a> were the most numerous of the Hispanic and Latino subgroups. Over 660,000 Puerto Ricans lived in New England in 2014, forming 4.5% of the population. The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dominican_American" title="Dominican American">Dominican</a> population is over 200,000, and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mexican_American" title="Mexican American">Mexican</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Guatemalan_American" title="Guatemalan American">Guatemalan</a> populations are each over 100,000.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hispanic_Latino_81-0"><a href="#cite_note-Hispanic_Latino-81">[80]</a></sup> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cuban_American" title="Cuban American">Americans of Cuban descent</a> are scant in number; there were roughly 26,000 Cuban Americans in the region in 2014. People of all other Hispanic and Latino ancestries, including <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Salvadoran_American" title="Salvadoran American">Salvadoran</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Colombian_American" title="Colombian American">Colombian</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bolivian_American" title="Bolivian American">Bolivian</a>, formed 2.5% of New England's population, and numbered over 361,000 combined.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hispanic_Latino_81-1"><a href="#cite_note-Hispanic_Latino-81">[80]</a></sup></p>
<p>According to the 2014 American Community Survey, the top ten largest reported European ancestries were the following:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82"><a href="#cite_note-82">[81]</a></sup></p>
<ul>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Irish_American" title="Irish American">Irish</a>: 19.2% (2.8 million)</li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Italian_American" title="Italian American">Italian</a>: 13.6% (2.0 million)</li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/French_American" title="French American">French</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/French_Canadian" title="French Canadian">French Canadian</a>: 13.1% (1.9 million)</li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/English_American" title="English American">English</a>: 11.9% (1.7 million)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83"><a href="#cite_note-83">[82]</a></sup></li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/German_American" title="German American">German</a>: 7.4% (1.1 million)</li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Polish_American" title="Polish American">Polish</a>: 4.9% (roughly 715,000)</li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Portuguese_American" title="Portuguese American">Portuguese</a>: 3.2% (467,000)</li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Scottish_American" title="Scottish American">Scottish</a>: 2.5% (370,000)</li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Russian_American" title="Russian American">Russian</a>: 1.4% (206,000)</li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Greek_American" title="Greek American">Greek</a>: 1.0% (152,000)</li>
</ul>
<p><a href="/wiki/English_language" title="English language">English</a> is, by far, the most common language spoken at home. Approximately 81.3% of all residents (11.3 million people) over the age of five spoke only English at home. Roughly 1,085,000 people (7.8% of the population) spoke Spanish at home, and roughly 970,000 people (7.0% of the population) spoke other <a href="/wiki/Indo-European_languages" title="Indo-European languages">Indo-European languages</a> at home. Over 403,000 people (2.9% of the population) spoke an <a href="/wiki/Languages_of_Asia" title="Languages of Asia">Asian</a> or Pacific Island language at home.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Language_84-0"><a href="#cite_note-Language-84">[83]</a></sup> Slightly fewer (about 1%) spoke French at home,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85"><a href="#cite_note-85">[84]</a></sup> although this figure is above 20% in northern New England, which borders francophone Québec.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Roughly 99,000 people (0.7% of the population) spoke languages other than these at home.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Language_84-1"><a href="#cite_note-Language-84">[83]</a></sup></p>
<p>As of 2014, approximately 87% of New England's inhabitants were born in the U.S., while over 12% were foreign-born.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-86"><a href="#cite_note-86">[85]</a></sup> 35.8% of foreign-born residents were born in Latin America, 28.6% were born in Asia, 22.9% were born in Europe, and 8.5% were born in Africa.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-87"><a href="#cite_note-87">[86]</a></sup></p>
<p>Southern New England forms an integral part of the <a href="/wiki/Northeast_megalopolis" title="Northeast megalopolis">BosWash</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Megalopolis_(city_type)" title="Megalopolis (city type)">megalopolis</a>, a conglomeration of urban centers that spans from Boston to Washington, D.C. The region includes three of the four <a href="/wiki/List_of_U.S._states_by_population_density" title="List of U.S. states by population density">most densely populated states in the U.S.</a>; only New Jersey has a higher population density than the states of Rhode Island, Massachusetts, and Connecticut.</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Greater_Boston" title="Greater Boston">Greater Boston</a>, which includes parts of southern New Hampshire, has a total population of approximately 4.8 million,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-metro_88-0"><a href="#cite_note-metro-88">[87]</a></sup> while over half the population of New England falls inside Boston's <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Combined_Statistical_Area" title="Combined Statistical Area">Combined Statistical Area</a> of over 8.2 million.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-89"><a href="#cite_note-89">[88]</a></sup></p>

<p>During the 20th century, urban expansion in regions surrounding <a href="/wiki/New_York_City" title="New York City">New York City</a> has become an important economic influence on neighboring Connecticut, parts of which belong to the <a href="/wiki/New_York_metropolitan_area" title="New York metropolitan area">New York metropolitan area</a>. The U.S. Census Bureau groups <a href="/wiki/Fairfield_County,_Connecticut" title="Fairfield County, Connecticut">Fairfield</a>, <a href="/wiki/New_Haven_County,_Connecticut" title="New Haven County, Connecticut">New Haven</a> and <a href="/wiki/Litchfield_County,_Connecticut" title="Litchfield County, Connecticut">Litchfield</a> counties in western Connecticut together with New York City, and other parts of New York and <a href="/wiki/New_Jersey" title="New Jersey">New Jersey</a> as a <a href="/wiki/Combined_statistical_area" title="Combined statistical area">combined statistical area</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-91"><a href="#cite_note-91">[90]</a></sup></p>
