<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=New_England&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Economy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_New_England" title="Economy of New England">Economy of New England</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Overview">Overview</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=New_England&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Overview">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:TheOldPort.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2592" data-file-width="3872" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b6/TheOldPort.jpg/220px-TheOldPort.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b6/TheOldPort.jpg/330px-TheOldPort.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b6/TheOldPort.jpg/440px-TheOldPort.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:TheOldPort.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Old Port (Wharf Street), in <a href="/wiki/Portland,_Maine" title="Portland, Maine">Portland, Maine</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Several factors combine to make the New England economy unique. The region is distant from the geographic center of the country, and is a relatively small region, and relatively densely populated. It historically has been an important center of industrial manufacturing and a supplier of natural resource products, such as <a href="/wiki/Granite" title="Granite">granite</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lobster" title="Lobster">lobster</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Codfish" title="Codfish">codfish</a>. New England exports food products, ranging from fish to lobster, cranberries, Maine potatoes, and <a href="/wiki/Maple_syrup" title="Maple syrup">maple syrup</a>. The service industry is important, including tourism, education, financial and insurance services, plus architectural, building, and construction services. The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/U.S._Department_of_Commerce" title="U.S. Department of Commerce">U.S. Department of Commerce</a> has called the New England economy a microcosm for the entire U.S. economy.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-USDOC1_92-0"><a href="#cite_note-USDOC1-92">[91]</a></sup></p>
<p>In the first half of the 20th century, the region underwent a long period of deindustrialization as traditional manufacturing companies relocated to the <a href="/wiki/Midwestern_United_States" title="Midwestern United States">Midwest</a>, with textile and furniture manufacturing migrating to the <a href="/wiki/Southern_United_States" title="Southern United States">South</a>. In the mid-to-late 20th century, an increasing portion of the regional economy included high technology (including computer and electronic equipment manufacturing), military defense industry, finance and insurance services, as well as education and health services.</p>
<p>As of 2015, the GDP of New England was $953.9 billion.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-93"><a href="#cite_note-93">[92]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Exports">Exports</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=New_England&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Exports">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Vermont_maple_syrup_in_a_tin_issued_by_the_Vermont_Maple_Sugar_Makers_Association.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1522" data-file-width="1167" height="222" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2d/Vermont_maple_syrup_in_a_tin_issued_by_the_Vermont_Maple_Sugar_Makers_Association.jpg/170px-Vermont_maple_syrup_in_a_tin_issued_by_the_Vermont_Maple_Sugar_Makers_Association.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2d/Vermont_maple_syrup_in_a_tin_issued_by_the_Vermont_Maple_Sugar_Makers_Association.jpg/255px-Vermont_maple_syrup_in_a_tin_issued_by_the_Vermont_Maple_Sugar_Makers_Association.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2d/Vermont_maple_syrup_in_a_tin_issued_by_the_Vermont_Maple_Sugar_Makers_Association.jpg/340px-Vermont_maple_syrup_in_a_tin_issued_by_the_Vermont_Maple_Sugar_Makers_Association.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Vermont_maple_syrup_in_a_tin_issued_by_the_Vermont_Maple_Sugar_Makers_Association.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Vermont <a href="/wiki/Maple_syrup" title="Maple syrup">maple syrup</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Exports consist mostly of industrial products, including specialized machines and <a href="/wiki/Weapon" title="Weapon">weaponry</a> (aircraft and missiles especially), built by the region's educated workforce. About half of the region's exports consist of industrial and commercial machinery, such as computers and electronic and electrical equipment. This, when combined with instruments, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Chemicals" title="Chemicals">chemicals</a>, and transportation equipment, makes up about three-quarters of the region's exports. Granite is quarried at <a href="/wiki/Barre_(town),_Vermont" title="Barre (town), Vermont">Barre, Vermont</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-94"><a href="#cite_note-94">[93]</a></sup> guns made at <a href="/wiki/Springfield,_Massachusetts" title="Springfield, Massachusetts">Springfield, Massachusetts</a> and <a href="/wiki/Saco,_Maine" title="Saco, Maine">Saco, Maine</a>, boats at <a href="/wiki/Groton,_Connecticut" title="Groton, Connecticut">Groton, Connecticut</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bath,_Maine" title="Bath, Maine">Bath, Maine</a>, and hand tools at <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Turners_Falls" title="Turners Falls">Turners Falls</a>, Massachusetts. Insurance is a driving force in and around <a href="/wiki/Hartford,_Connecticut" title="Hartford, Connecticut">Hartford, Connecticut</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-USDOC1_92-1"><a href="#cite_note-USDOC1-92">[91]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Agriculture">Agriculture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=New_England&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Agriculture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Agriculture is limited by the area's rocky soil, cool climate, and small area. Some New England states, however, are ranked highly among U.S. states for particular areas of production. Maine is ranked ninth for <a href="/wiki/Aquaculture" title="Aquaculture">aquaculture</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-95"><a href="#cite_note-95">[94]</a></sup> and has abundant potato fields in its northeast part. Vermont is fifteenth for dairy products,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-96"><a href="#cite_note-96">[95]</a></sup> and Connecticut and Massachusetts seventh and eleventh for tobacco, respectively.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-97"><a href="#cite_note-97">[96]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-98"><a href="#cite_note-98">[97]</a></sup> Cranberries are grown in Massachusetts' <a href="/wiki/Cape_Cod" title="Cape Cod">Cape Cod</a>-Plymouth-South Shore area, and blueberries in Maine.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Energy">Energy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=New_England&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Energy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Seabrook_2009-2.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="683" data-file-width="1024" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5f/Seabrook_2009-2.jpg/220px-Seabrook_2009-2.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5f/Seabrook_2009-2.jpg/330px-Seabrook_2009-2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5f/Seabrook_2009-2.jpg/440px-Seabrook_2009-2.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Seabrook_2009-2.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Seabrook_Station_Nuclear_Power_Plant" title="Seabrook Station Nuclear Power Plant">Seabrook Station Nuclear Power Plant</a> in <a href="/wiki/Seabrook,_New_Hampshire" title="Seabrook, New Hampshire">Seabrook, New Hampshire</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Three of the six New England states are among the country's highest consumers of nuclear power: Vermont (first, 73.7%), Connecticut (fourth, 48.9%), and New Hampshire (sixth, 46%).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-99"><a href="#cite_note-99">[98]</a></sup> The region is mostly energy-efficient compared to the U.S. at large, with every state but Maine ranking within the ten most energy-efficient states;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-100"><a href="#cite_note-100">[99]</a></sup> every state in New England also ranks within the ten most expensive states for electricity prices.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-101"><a href="#cite_note-101">[100]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Employment">Employment</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=New_England&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Employment">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>

<p>As of January 2017, employment is stronger in New England than in the rest of the United States. During the <a href="/wiki/Great_Recession" title="Great Recession">Great Recession</a>, unemployment rates ballooned across New England as elsewhere; however, in the years that followed, these rates declined steadily, with New Hampshire and Massachusetts having the lowest unemployment rates in the country, respectively. The most extreme swing was in Rhode Island, which had an unemployment rate above 10% following the recession, but which saw this rate decline by over 6% in six years.</p>
<p>As of December 2016, the <a href="/wiki/Metropolitan_statistical_area" title="Metropolitan statistical area">metropolitan statistical area</a> (MSA) with the lowest unemployment rate, 2.1%, was <a href="/wiki/Burlington,_Vermont" title="Burlington, Vermont">Burlington-South Burlington, Vermont</a>; the MSA with the highest rate, 4.9%, was <a href="/wiki/Waterbury,_Connecticut" title="Waterbury, Connecticut">Waterbury, Connecticut</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-104"><a href="#cite_note-104">[103]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Government">Government</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=New_England&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Government">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Government_of_Vermont" title="Government of Vermont">Government of Vermont</a>, <a href="/wiki/Government_of_New_Hampshire" title="Government of New Hampshire">Government of New Hampshire</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Government_of_Maine" title="Government of Maine">Government of Maine</a>, <a href="/wiki/Government_of_Massachusetts" title="Government of Massachusetts">Government of Massachusetts</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Government_of_Connecticut" title="Government of Connecticut">Government of Connecticut</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Government_of_Rhode_Island" title="Government of Rhode Island">Government of Rhode Island</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Town_meetings">Town meetings</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=New_England&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Town meetings">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Town_meeting" title="Town meeting">Town meeting</a> and <a href="/wiki/New_England_town" title="New England town">New England town</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Huntington_town_meeting.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2048" data-file-width="3072" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Huntington_town_meeting.jpg/220px-Huntington_town_meeting.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Huntington_town_meeting.jpg/330px-Huntington_town_meeting.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Huntington_town_meeting.jpg/440px-Huntington_town_meeting.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Huntington_town_meeting.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
A <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/New_England_town_meeting" title="New England town meeting">New England town meeting</a> in <a href="/wiki/Huntington,_Vermont" title="Huntington, Vermont">Huntington, Vermont</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/New_England_town_meeting" title="New England town meeting">New England town meetings</a> were derived from meetings held by church elders, and are still an integral part of government in many <a href="/wiki/New_England_town" title="New England town">New England towns</a>. At such meetings, any citizen of the town may discuss issues with other members of the community and vote on them. This is the strongest example of <a href="/wiki/Direct_democracy" title="Direct democracy">direct democracy</a> in the U.S. today, and the strong democratic tradition was even apparent in the early 19th century, when <a href="/wiki/Alexis_de_Tocqueville" title="Alexis de Tocqueville">Alexis de Tocqueville</a> wrote in <i><a href="/wiki/Democracy_in_America" title="Democracy in America">Democracy in America</a></i>:</p>
<table class="cquote" role="presentation" style="margin:auto; border-collapse: collapse; border: none; background-color: transparent; width: auto;">
<tr>
<td style="width: 20px; vertical-align: top; border: none; color: #B2B7F2; font-size: 40px; font-family: 'Times New Roman', Times, serif; font-weight: bold; line-height: .6em; text-align: left; padding: 10px 10px;">“</td>
<td style="vertical-align: top; border: none; padding: 4px 10px;">New England, where education and liberty are the daughters of morality and religion, where society has acquired age and stability enough to enable it to form principles and hold fixed habits, the common people are accustomed to respect intellectual and moral superiority and to submit to it without complaint, although they set at naught all those privileges which wealth and birth have introduced among mankind. In New England, consequently, the democracy makes a more judicious choice than it does elsewhere.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-105"><a href="#cite_note-105">[104]</a></sup></td>
<td style="width: 20px; vertical-align: bottom; border: none; color: #B2B7F2; font-size: 40px; font-family: 'Times New Roman', Times, serif; font-weight: bold; line-height: .6em; text-align: right; padding: 10px 10px;">”</td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>By contrast, <a href="/wiki/James_Madison" title="James Madison">James Madison</a> wrote in <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Federalist_Papers" title="Federalist Papers">Federalist No. 55</a></i> that, regardless of the assembly, "passion never fails to wrest the scepter from reason. Had every Athenian citizen been a Socrates, every Athenian assembly would still have been a mob."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-106"><a href="#cite_note-106">[105]</a></sup> The use and effectiveness of town meetings is still discussed by scholars, as well as the possible application of the format to other regions and countries.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-107"><a href="#cite_note-107">[106]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Politics">Politics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=New_England&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Politics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Politics_of_New_England" title="Politics of New England">Politics of New England</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Elections">Elections</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=New_England&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Elections">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Elections_in_New_England" title="Elections in New England">Elections in New England</a></div>
<p>State and national elected officials in New England recently have been elected mainly from the Democratic Party.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-108"><a href="#cite_note-108">[107]</a></sup> The region is generally considered to be the most liberal in the United States, with more New Englanders identifying as liberals than Americans elsewhere. In 2010, four of six of the New England states were polled as the most liberal in the United States; Maine and New Hampshire also were more liberal than the bottom-half.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-109"><a href="#cite_note-109">[108]</a></sup></p>
<p>The six states of New England voted for the Democratic <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/United_States_Presidential_Elections" title="United States Presidential Elections">Presidential nominee</a> in the 1992, 1996, 2004, 2008, 2012, and 2016 elections, and every New England state other than New Hampshire voted for <a href="/wiki/Al_Gore" title="Al Gore">Al Gore</a> in the <a href="/wiki/United_States_presidential_election,_2000" title="United States presidential election, 2000">presidential election of 2000</a>. In the <a href="/wiki/113th_United_States_Congress" title="113th United States Congress">113th Congress</a> the <a href="/wiki/United_States_House_of_Representatives" title="United States House of Representatives">House delegations</a> from all six states of New England were all Democratic. New England is home to the only two independents currently serving in the U.S. Senate, both of whom caucus with the Democratic Party: <a href="/wiki/Bernie_Sanders" title="Bernie Sanders">Bernie Sanders</a>, a self-described <a href="/wiki/Democratic_socialism" title="Democratic socialism">democratic socialist</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-socialistsuccess_110-0"><a href="#cite_note-socialistsuccess-110">[109]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-politicosocialist_111-0"><a href="#cite_note-politicosocialist-111">[110]</a></sup> representing <a href="/wiki/Vermont" title="Vermont">Vermont</a>; and <a href="/wiki/Angus_King" title="Angus King">Angus King</a>, an Independent representing Maine.</p>
<p>In the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/U.S._presidential_election,_2008" title="U.S. presidential election, 2008">2008 presidential election</a>, Barack Obama carried all six New England states by 9 percentage points or more.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-112"><a href="#cite_note-112">[111]</a></sup> He carried every county in New England except for <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Piscataquis_County" title="Piscataquis County">Piscataquis County</a>, <a href="/wiki/Maine" title="Maine">Maine</a>, which he lost by 4% to Senator <a href="/wiki/John_McCain" title="John McCain">John McCain</a> (R-AZ). Pursuant to the reapportionment following the 2010 census, New England collectively has 33 <a href="/wiki/Electoral_College_(United_States)" title="Electoral College (United States)">electoral votes</a>.</p>

<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Political_party_strength">Political party strength</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=New_England&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Political party strength">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Judging purely by party registration rather than voting patterns, New England today is one of the most Democratic regions in the U.S.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-113"><a href="#cite_note-113">[112]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-114"><a href="#cite_note-114">[113]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-115"><a href="#cite_note-115">[114]</a></sup> According to <a href="/wiki/Gallup_(company)" title="Gallup (company)">Gallup</a>, <a href="/wiki/Connecticut" title="Connecticut">Connecticut</a>, <a href="/wiki/Massachusetts" title="Massachusetts">Massachusetts</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rhode_Island" title="Rhode Island">Rhode Island</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Vermont" title="Vermont">Vermont</a> are "solidly Democratic", <a href="/wiki/Maine" title="Maine">Maine</a> "leans Democratic", and <a href="/wiki/New_Hampshire" title="New Hampshire">New Hampshire</a> is a swing state.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-116"><a href="#cite_note-116">[115]</a></sup> Though New England is today considered a Democratic Party stronghold, much of the region was staunchly Republican before the mid-twentieth century. This changed in the late 20th century, in large part due to demographic shifts<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-117"><a href="#cite_note-117">[116]</a></sup> and the Republican Party's adoption of socially conservative platforms as part of their strategic <a href="/wiki/Southern_strategy" title="Southern strategy">shift towards the South</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tarr_60-1"><a href="#cite_note-tarr-60">[59]</a></sup> For example, Vermont voted Republican in every presidential election but one from 1856 through 1988, and has voted Democratic every election since. Maine and Vermont were the only two states in the nation to vote against Democrat <a href="/wiki/Franklin_D._Roosevelt" title="Franklin D. Roosevelt">Franklin D. Roosevelt</a> all four times he ran for president. Republicans in New England are today considered by both liberals and conservatives to be <a href="/wiki/Rockefeller_Republican" title="Rockefeller Republican">more moderate</a> (socially liberal) compared to Republicans in other parts of the U.S.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-118"><a href="#cite_note-118">[117]</a></sup></p>
<dl>
<dd><span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_independent.E2.80.A0"><a href="#ref_independent.E2.80.A0"><b><sup>†</sup></b></a></span> Elected as an independent, but caucuses with the Democratic Party.</dd>
</dl>
