Alumni Hall at <a href="/wiki/Saint_Anselm_College" title="Saint Anselm College">Saint Anselm College</a> has served as a backdrop for the media reports during the <a href="/wiki/New_Hampshire_primary" title="New Hampshire primary">New Hampshire primary</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="New_Hampshire_primary">New Hampshire primary</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=New_England&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: New Hampshire primary">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/New_Hampshire_primary" title="New Hampshire primary">New Hampshire primary</a></div>
<p>Historically, the <a href="/wiki/New_Hampshire_primary" title="New Hampshire primary">New Hampshire primary</a> has been the first in a series of nationwide political party <a href="/wiki/Primary_election" title="Primary election">primary elections</a> held in the United States every four years. Held in the state of <a href="/wiki/New_Hampshire" title="New Hampshire">New Hampshire</a>, it usually marks the beginning of the <a href="/wiki/United_States_presidential_election" title="United States presidential election">U.S. presidential election</a> process. Even though few delegates are chosen from New Hampshire, the primary has always been pivotal to both New England and American politics. One college in particular, <a href="/wiki/Saint_Anselm_College" title="Saint Anselm College">Saint Anselm College</a>, has been home to numerous national presidential debates and visits by candidates to its campus.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-119"><a href="#cite_note-119">[118]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=New_England&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Colleges_and_universities">Colleges and universities</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=New_England&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: Colleges and universities">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Dartmouth-hall.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="800" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fb/Dartmouth-hall.jpg/220px-Dartmouth-hall.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fb/Dartmouth-hall.jpg/330px-Dartmouth-hall.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fb/Dartmouth-hall.jpg/440px-Dartmouth-hall.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Dartmouth-hall.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
New England is home to four of the eight <a href="/wiki/Ivy_League" title="Ivy League">Ivy League</a> universities. Pictured here is Dartmouth Hall on the campus of <a href="/wiki/Dartmouth_College" title="Dartmouth College">Dartmouth College</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>New England contains some of the oldest and most renowned institutions of higher learning in the United States and the world. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Harvard" title="Harvard">Harvard College</a> was the first such institution, founded in 1636 at <a href="/wiki/Cambridge,_Massachusetts" title="Cambridge, Massachusetts">Cambridge, Massachusetts</a> to train preachers. <a href="/wiki/Yale_University" title="Yale University">Yale University</a> was founded in <a href="/wiki/Old_Saybrook,_Connecticut" title="Old Saybrook, Connecticut">Saybrook</a>, <a href="/wiki/Connecticut" title="Connecticut">Connecticut</a> in 1701, and awarded the nation's first doctoral (PhD) degree in 1861. Yale moved to <a href="/wiki/New_Haven,_Connecticut" title="New Haven, Connecticut">New Haven, Connecticut</a> in 1718, where it has remained to the present day.</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Brown_University" title="Brown University">Brown University</a> was the first college in the nation to accept students of all religious affiliations, and is the seventh oldest U.S. institution of higher learning. It was founded in <a href="/wiki/Providence,_Rhode_Island" title="Providence, Rhode Island">Providence, Rhode Island</a> in 1764. <a href="/wiki/Dartmouth_College" title="Dartmouth College">Dartmouth College</a> was founded five years later in <a href="/wiki/Hanover,_New_Hampshire" title="Hanover, New Hampshire">Hanover, New Hampshire</a> with the mission of educating the local <a href="/wiki/Native_Americans_in_the_United_States" title="Native Americans in the United States">American Indian</a> population as well as English youth. The <a href="/wiki/University_of_Vermont" title="University of Vermont">University of Vermont</a>, the fifth oldest university in New England, was founded in 1791, the same year that Vermont joined the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/United_States_of_America" title="United States of America">Union</a>.</p>
<p>In addition to four out of eight <a href="/wiki/Ivy_League" title="Ivy League">Ivy League</a> schools, New England contains the <a href="/wiki/Massachusetts_Institute_of_Technology" title="Massachusetts Institute of Technology">Massachusetts Institute of Technology</a> (MIT), four of the original <a href="/wiki/Seven_Sisters_(colleges)" title="Seven Sisters (colleges)">Seven Sisters</a>, the bulk of educational institutions that are identified as the "<a href="/wiki/Little_Ivies" title="Little Ivies">Little Ivies</a>", one of the eight original <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Public_Ivies" title="Public Ivies">Public Ivies</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Colleges_of_Worcester_Consortium" title="Colleges of Worcester Consortium">Colleges of Worcester Consortium</a> in central Massachusetts, and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Five_Colleges_(Massachusetts)" title="Five Colleges (Massachusetts)">Five Colleges</a> consortium in western Massachusetts. The <a href="/wiki/University_of_Maine" title="University of Maine">University of Maine</a>, the <a href="/wiki/University_of_New_Hampshire" title="University of New Hampshire">University of New Hampshire</a>, the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Connecticut" title="University of Connecticut">University of Connecticut</a>, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/University_of_Massachusetts_at_Amherst" title="University of Massachusetts at Amherst">University of Massachusetts at Amherst</a>, the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Rhode_Island" title="University of Rhode Island">University of Rhode Island</a>, and the University of Vermont are the flagship state universities in the region.</p>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_colleges_and_universities_in_Connecticut" title="List of colleges and universities in Connecticut">List of colleges and universities in Connecticut</a>, <a href="/wiki/List_of_colleges_and_universities_in_Maine" title="List of colleges and universities in Maine">List of colleges and universities in Maine</a>, <a href="/wiki/List_of_colleges_and_universities_in_Massachusetts" title="List of colleges and universities in Massachusetts">List of colleges and universities in Massachusetts</a>, <a href="/wiki/List_of_colleges_and_universities_in_New_Hampshire" title="List of colleges and universities in New Hampshire">List of colleges and universities in New Hampshire</a>, <a href="/wiki/List_of_colleges_and_universities_in_Rhode_Island" title="List of colleges and universities in Rhode Island">List of colleges and universities in Rhode Island</a>, and <a href="/wiki/List_of_colleges_and_universities_in_Vermont" title="List of colleges and universities in Vermont">List of colleges and universities in Vermont</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Private_and_independent_secondary_schools">Private and independent secondary schools</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=New_England&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: Private and independent secondary schools">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>At the pre-college level, New England is home to a number of American independent schools (also known as private schools). The concept of the elite "New England <a href="/wiki/University-preparatory_school" title="University-preparatory school">prep school</a>" (preparatory school) and the "<a href="/wiki/Preppy" title="Preppy">preppy</a>" lifestyle is an iconic part of the region's image.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-120"><a href="#cite_note-120">[119]</a></sup></p>
<dl>
<dd>See the list of private schools for each state:<br/>
<a href="/wiki/Category:Private_schools_in_Connecticut" title="Category:Private schools in Connecticut">Connecticut</a>, <a href="/wiki/Category:Private_schools_in_Massachusetts" title="Category:Private schools in Massachusetts">Massachusetts</a>, <a href="/wiki/Category:Private_schools_in_Maine" title="Category:Private schools in Maine">Maine</a>, <a href="/wiki/Category:Private_schools_in_New_Hampshire" title="Category:Private schools in New Hampshire">New Hampshire</a>, <a href="/wiki/Category:Private_schools_in_Rhode_Island" title="Category:Private schools in Rhode Island">Rhode Island</a>, <a href="/wiki/Category:Private_schools_in_Vermont" title="Category:Private schools in Vermont">Vermont</a>.</dd>
</dl>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Public_education">Public education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=New_England&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: Public education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Latin_Public_School.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1728" data-file-width="2304" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7a/Latin_Public_School.jpg/220px-Latin_Public_School.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7a/Latin_Public_School.jpg/330px-Latin_Public_School.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7a/Latin_Public_School.jpg/440px-Latin_Public_School.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Latin_Public_School.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Boston_Latin_School" title="Boston Latin School">Boston Latin School</a> is the oldest public school in the U.S., established in 1635.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>New England is home to some of the oldest public schools in the nation. <a href="/wiki/Boston_Latin_School" title="Boston Latin School">Boston Latin School</a> is the oldest public school in America and was attended by several signatories of the Declaration of Independence.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-121"><a href="#cite_note-121">[120]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Hartford_Public_High_School" title="Hartford Public High School">Hartford Public High School</a> is the second oldest operating high school in the U.S.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-122"><a href="#cite_note-122">[121]</a></sup></p>
<p>As of 2005, the <a href="/wiki/National_Education_Association" title="National Education Association">National Education Association</a> ranked Connecticut as having the highest-paid teachers in the country. Massachusetts and Rhode Island ranked eighth and ninth, respectively.</p>
<p>New Hampshire, Rhode Island, and Vermont have cooperated in developing a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/New_England_Common_Assessment_Program" title="New England Common Assessment Program">New England Common Assessment Program</a> test under the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/No_Child_Left_Behind" title="No Child Left Behind">No Child Left Behind</a> guidelines. These states can compare the resultant scores with each other.</p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Maine_Learning_Technology_Initiative" title="Maine Learning Technology Initiative">Maine Learning Technology Initiative</a> program supplies all students with <a href="/wiki/Apple_Inc." title="Apple Inc.">Apple</a> <a href="/wiki/MacBook" title="MacBook">MacBook</a> laptops.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Academic_journals_and_press">Academic journals and press</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=New_England&amp;action=edit&amp;section=39" title="Edit section: Academic journals and press">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>There are several academic journals and publishing companies in the region, including <i><a href="/wiki/The_New_England_Journal_of_Medicine" title="The New England Journal of Medicine">The New England Journal of Medicine</a></i>, <a href="/wiki/Harvard_University_Press" title="Harvard University Press">Harvard University Press</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Yale_University_Press" title="Yale University Press">Yale University Press</a>. Some of its institutions lead the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Open_access_(publishing)" title="Open access (publishing)">open access</a> alternative to conventional academic publication, including <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/MIT" title="MIT">MIT</a>, the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Connecticut" title="University of Connecticut">University of Connecticut</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Maine" title="University of Maine">University of Maine</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Federal_Reserve_Bank_of_Boston" title="Federal Reserve Bank of Boston">Federal Reserve Bank of Boston</a> publishes the <i>New England Economic Review</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-123"><a href="#cite_note-123">[122]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=New_England&amp;action=edit&amp;section=40" title="Edit section: Culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Cushing_house_Hingham_Massachusetts.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="825" data-file-width="1024" height="177" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6b/Cushing_house_Hingham_Massachusetts.jpg/220px-Cushing_house_Hingham_Massachusetts.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6b/Cushing_house_Hingham_Massachusetts.jpg/330px-Cushing_house_Hingham_Massachusetts.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6b/Cushing_house_Hingham_Massachusetts.jpg/440px-Cushing_house_Hingham_Massachusetts.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Cushing_house_Hingham_Massachusetts.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Cushing house, <a href="/wiki/Hingham,_Massachusetts" title="Hingham, Massachusetts">Hingham, Massachusetts</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Peacham,_Vermont_Church.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1024" data-file-width="768" height="293" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/20/Peacham%2C_Vermont_Church.jpg/220px-Peacham%2C_Vermont_Church.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/20/Peacham%2C_Vermont_Church.jpg/330px-Peacham%2C_Vermont_Church.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/20/Peacham%2C_Vermont_Church.jpg/440px-Peacham%2C_Vermont_Church.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Peacham,_Vermont_Church.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Classic New England Congregationalist church in <a href="/wiki/Peacham,_Vermont" title="Peacham, Vermont">Peacham, Vermont</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>New England has a shared heritage and culture primarily shaped by waves of immigration from Europe.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-124"><a href="#cite_note-124">[123]</a></sup> In contrast to other American regions, many of New England's earliest Puritan settlers came from eastern England, contributing to New England's distinctive accents, foods, customs, and social structures.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hackett_Fischer_125-0"><a href="#cite_note-Hackett_Fischer-125">[124]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:30–50</sup> Within modern New England a cultural divide exists between urban New Englanders living along the densely populated coastline, and rural New Englanders in western Massachusetts, northwestern and northeastern Connecticut, Vermont, New Hampshire, and Maine, where population density is low.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-126"><a href="#cite_note-126">[125]</a></sup></p>
<p>Today, New England is the least religious region of the U.S. In 2009, less than half of those polled in Maine, Massachusetts, New Hampshire, and Vermont claimed that religion was an important part of their daily lives. In Connecticut and Rhode Island, also among the ten least religious states, 55 and 53%, respectively, of those polled claimed that it was.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-127"><a href="#cite_note-127">[126]</a></sup> According to the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/American_Religious_Identification_Survey" title="American Religious Identification Survey">American Religious Identification Survey</a>, 34% of Vermonters, a plurality, claimed to have no religion; on average, nearly one out of every four New Englanders identifies as having no religion, more than in any other part of the U.S.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ARIS2008_128-0"><a href="#cite_note-ARIS2008-128">[127]</a></sup> New England had one of the highest percentages of Catholics in the U.S. This number declined from 50% in 1990 to 36% in 2008.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ARIS2008_128-1"><a href="#cite_note-ARIS2008-128">[127]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cultural_roots">Cultural roots</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=New_England&amp;action=edit&amp;section=41" title="Edit section: Cultural roots">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Many of the first European colonists of New England had a <a href="/wiki/Sea" title="Sea">maritime</a> orientation toward <a href="/wiki/Whaling" title="Whaling">whaling</a> (first noted about 1650)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-129"><a href="#cite_note-129">[128]</a></sup> and fishing, in addition to farming. New England has developed a distinct <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/New_England_cuisine" title="New England cuisine">cuisine</a>, <a href="/wiki/Eastern_New_England_English" title="Eastern New England English">dialect</a>, <a href="/wiki/Connected_farm" title="Connected farm">architecture</a>, and government. New England cuisine has a reputation for its emphasis on seafood and dairy; <a href="/wiki/Clam_chowder" title="Clam chowder">clam chowder</a>, lobster, and other products of the sea are among some of the region's most popular foods.</p>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Cuisine_of_New_England" title="Cuisine of New England">Cuisine of New England</a></div>
<p>New England has largely preserved its regional character, especially in its historic places. The region has become more <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ethnic_diversity" title="Ethnic diversity">ethnically diverse</a>, having seen waves of immigration from Ireland, Quebec, Italy, Portugal, Poland, Asia, Latin America, Africa, other parts of the U.S., and elsewhere. The enduring European influence can be seen in the region in the use of traffic <a href="/wiki/Roundabout" title="Roundabout">rotaries</a>, the bilingual French and English towns of northern Vermont, Maine, and New Hampshire, the region's heavy prevalence of English town- and county-names, and its unique, often non-<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rhotic_and_non-rhotic_accents" title="Rhotic and non-rhotic accents">rhotic</a> coastal dialect reminiscent of southeastern England.</p>
<p>Within New England, many names of towns (and a few counties) repeat from state to state, primarily due to settlers throughout the region having named their new towns after their old ones. For example, the town of <a href="/wiki/North_Yarmouth,_Maine" title="North Yarmouth, Maine">North Yarmouth, Maine</a> was named by settlers from <a href="/wiki/Yarmouth,_Massachusetts" title="Yarmouth, Massachusetts">Yarmouth, Massachusetts</a>, which was in turn named for <a href="/wiki/Great_Yarmouth" title="Great Yarmouth">Great Yarmouth</a> in England. As another example, every New England state has a town named Warren, and every state except Rhode Island has a city or town named Andover, Bridgewater, Chester, Franklin, Manchester, Plymouth, Washington, and Windsor; in addition, every state except Connecticut has a Lincoln and a Richmond, and Massachusetts, Vermont, and Maine each contains a <a class="mw-redirect mw-disambig" href="/wiki/Franklin_County_(disambiguation)" title="Franklin County (disambiguation)">Franklin County</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Accents">Accents</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=New_England&amp;action=edit&amp;section=42" title="Edit section: Accents">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<table class="plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Refimprove" role="presentation">
<tr>
<td class="mbox-image">
<div style="width:52px"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg"><img alt="" data-file-height="399" data-file-width="512" height="39" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" width="50"/></a></div>
</td>
<td class="mbox-text">
<div class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>needs additional citations for <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">verification</a></b>. <span class="hide-when-compact">Please help <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=New_England&amp;action=edit">improve this article</a> by <a href="/wiki/Help:Introduction_to_referencing_with_Wiki_Markup/1" title="Help:Introduction to referencing with Wiki Markup/1">adding citations to reliable sources</a>. Unsourced material may be challenged and removed.</span> <small><i>(November 2016)</i></small> <small class="hide-when-compact"><i>(<a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a>)</i></small></div>
</td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>There are several <a href="/wiki/American_English" title="American English">American English</a> accents spoken in the region, including <a href="/wiki/New_England_English" title="New England English">New England English</a> and its derivative known as the <a href="/wiki/Boston_accent" title="Boston accent">Boston accent</a>.</p>
<p>The so-called Boston accent is native to the northeastern coastal regions of New England. Many of its most identifiable features are believed to have originated from the influence of England's <a href="/wiki/Received_Pronunciation" title="Received Pronunciation">Received Pronunciation</a>, which shares those features, such as <a href="/wiki/Rhoticity_in_English" title="Rhoticity in English">dropping final R</a> and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Broad_A" title="Broad A">broad A</a>. Another source was 17th century speech in <a href="/wiki/East_Anglia" title="East Anglia">East Anglia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Lincolnshire" title="Lincolnshire">Lincolnshire</a> where many of the Puritan immigrants originated. The East Anglian "whine" developed into the Yankee "twang".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hackett_Fischer_125-1"><a href="#cite_note-Hackett_Fischer-125">[124]</a></sup> Boston accents were most strongly associated at one point with the so-called "<a href="/wiki/The_Establishment" title="The Establishment">Eastern Establishment</a>" and <a href="/wiki/Boston_Brahmin" title="Boston Brahmin">Boston's upper class</a>, although today the accent is predominantly associated with blue-collar natives, as exemplified by movies such as <i><a href="/wiki/Good_Will_Hunting" title="Good Will Hunting">Good Will Hunting</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/The_Departed" title="The Departed">The Departed</a></i>. The Boston accent and those accents closely related to it cover eastern Massachusetts, New Hampshire, and Maine.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-130"><a href="#cite_note-130">[129]</a></sup></p>
<p>Some Rhode Islanders speak with a <a href="/wiki/Rhoticity_in_English" title="Rhoticity in English">non-rhotic</a> accent that many compare to a "<a href="/wiki/Brooklyn" title="Brooklyn">Brooklyn</a>" accent or a cross between a New York and <a href="/wiki/Boston_accent" title="Boston accent">Boston accent</a>, where "water" becomes "wata". Many Rhode Islanders distinguish the <i>aw</i> sound <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[<a href="/wiki/Open-mid_back_rounded_vowel" title="Open-mid back rounded vowel">ɔː</a>]</span>, as one might hear in <a href="/wiki/New_Jersey" title="New Jersey">New Jersey</a>; e.g., the word "coffee" is pronounced <span class="nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="'k' in 'kind'">k</span><span title="/ɔː/: 'au' in 'fraud'">ɔː</span><span title="'f' in 'find'">f</span><span title="/iː/ or /ɪ/: 'y' in 'happy'">i</span></span>/</a></span></span> <a href="/wiki/Help:Pronunciation_respelling_key" title="Help:Pronunciation respelling key"><small title="English pronunciation respelling"><i><b>KAW</b>-fee</i></small></a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rilang_131-0"><a href="#cite_note-rilang-131">[130]</a></sup> This type of accent was brought to the region by early settlers from eastern England in the Puritan migration in the mid-seventeenth century.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hackett_Fischer_125-2"><a href="#cite_note-Hackett_Fischer-125">[124]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:13–207</sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Social_activities_and_music">Social activities and music</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=New_England&amp;action=edit&amp;section=43" title="Edit section: Social activities and music">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Acadian" title="Acadian">Acadian</a> and <a href="/wiki/French-speaking_Quebecer" title="French-speaking Quebecer">Québécois</a> culture are included in music and dance in much of rural New England, particularly Maine. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Contra_dancing" title="Contra dancing">Contra dancing</a> and country <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Square_dancing" title="Square dancing">square dancing</a> are popular throughout New England, usually backed by live Irish, Acadian, or other folk music. <a href="/wiki/Fife_and_drum_corps" title="Fife and drum corps">Fife and drum corps</a> are common, especially in southern New England and more specifically <a href="/wiki/Connecticut" title="Connecticut">Connecticut</a>, with music of mostly Celtic, English, and local origin.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:HPIM0003.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1968" data-file-width="2624" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b6/HPIM0003.JPG/220px-HPIM0003.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b6/HPIM0003.JPG/330px-HPIM0003.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b6/HPIM0003.JPG/440px-HPIM0003.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:HPIM0003.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Opera houses and theaters are popular in New England towns, such as the Vergennes Opera House in <a href="/wiki/Vergennes,_Vermont" title="Vergennes, Vermont">Vergennes, Vermont</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Traditional <a href="/wiki/Knitting" title="Knitting">knitting</a>, <a href="/wiki/Quilting" title="Quilting">quilting</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Traditional_Rug_Hooking" title="Traditional Rug Hooking">rug hooking</a> circles in rural New England have become less common; <a href="/wiki/Church_service" title="Church service">church</a>, sports, and <a href="/wiki/Town_meeting" title="Town meeting">town government</a> are more typical social activities. These traditional gatherings are often hosted in individual homes or civic centers.</p>
<p>New England leads the U.S. in ice cream consumption per capita.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-132"><a href="#cite_note-132">[131]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-133"><a href="#cite_note-133">[132]</a></sup> In the U.S., <a href="/wiki/Candlepin_bowling" title="Candlepin bowling">candlepin bowling</a> is essentially confined to New England, where it was invented in the 19th century.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-134"><a href="#cite_note-134">[133]</a></sup></p>
<p>New England was an important center of <a href="/wiki/American_classical_music" title="American classical music">American classical music</a> for some time. Prominent <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Musical_modernism" title="Musical modernism">modernist</a> composers also come from the region, including <a href="/wiki/Charles_Ives" title="Charles Ives">Charles Ives</a> and <a href="/wiki/John_Adams_(composer)" title="John Adams (composer)">John Adams</a>. Boston is the site of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/New_England_Conservatory" title="New England Conservatory">New England Conservatory</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Boston_Symphony_Orchestra" title="Boston Symphony Orchestra">Boston Symphony Orchestra</a>.</p>
<p>In popular music, the region has produced <a href="/wiki/Donna_Summer" title="Donna Summer">Donna Summer</a>, <a href="/wiki/JoJo_(singer)" title="JoJo (singer)">JoJo</a>, New Edition, <a href="/wiki/Bobby_Brown" title="Bobby Brown">Bobby Brown</a>, <a href="/wiki/Passion_Pit" title="Passion Pit">Passion Pit</a>, <a href="/wiki/Meghan_Trainor" title="Meghan Trainor">Meghan Trainor</a>, <a href="/wiki/New_Kids_on_the_Block" title="New Kids on the Block">New Kids on the Block</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rachel_Platten" title="Rachel Platten">Rachel Platten</a>, and <a href="/wiki/John_Mayer" title="John Mayer">John Mayer</a>. In rock music, the region has produced <a href="/wiki/Rob_Zombie" title="Rob Zombie">Rob Zombie</a>, <a href="/wiki/Aerosmith" title="Aerosmith">Aerosmith</a>, <a href="/wiki/The_Modern_Lovers" title="The Modern Lovers">The Modern Lovers</a>, <a href="/wiki/Phish" title="Phish">Phish</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Pixies" title="Pixies">Pixies</a>, <a href="/wiki/GG_Allin" title="GG Allin">GG Allin</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Dropkick_Murphys" title="Dropkick Murphys">Dropkick Murphys</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Boston_(band)" title="Boston (band)">Boston</a>. <a href="/wiki/Quincy,_Massachusetts" title="Quincy, Massachusetts">Quincy, Massachusetts</a> native <a href="/wiki/Dick_Dale" title="Dick Dale">Dick Dale</a> helped popularize <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Surf_rock" title="Surf rock">surf rock</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Media">Media</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=New_England&amp;action=edit&amp;section=44" title="Edit section: Media">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The leading U.S. cable TV sports broadcaster <a href="/wiki/ESPN" title="ESPN">ESPN</a> is headquartered in <a href="/wiki/Bristol,_Connecticut" title="Bristol, Connecticut">Bristol, Connecticut</a>. New England has several regional cable networks, including <a href="/wiki/New_England_Cable_News" title="New England Cable News">New England Cable News</a> (NECN) and the <a href="/wiki/New_England_Sports_Network" title="New England Sports Network">New England Sports Network</a> (NESN). New England Cable News is the largest regional <a href="/wiki/24-hour_news_cycle" title="24-hour news cycle">24-hour</a> <a href="/wiki/United_States_cable_news" title="United States cable news">cable news</a> network in the U.S., broadcasting to more than 3.2 million homes in all of the New England states. Its studios are located in <a href="/wiki/Newton,_Massachusetts" title="Newton, Massachusetts">Newton, Massachusetts</a>, outside of Boston, and it maintains bureaus in <a href="/wiki/Manchester,_New_Hampshire" title="Manchester, New Hampshire">Manchester, New Hampshire</a>; <a href="/wiki/Hartford,_Connecticut" title="Hartford, Connecticut">Hartford, Connecticut</a>; <a href="/wiki/Worcester,_Massachusetts" title="Worcester, Massachusetts">Worcester, Massachusetts</a>; <a href="/wiki/Portland,_Maine" title="Portland, Maine">Portland, Maine</a>; and <a href="/wiki/Burlington,_Vermont" title="Burlington, Vermont">Burlington, Vermont</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-135"><a href="#cite_note-135">[134]</a></sup> In Connecticut, Litchfield, Fairfield, and New Haven counties it also broadcasts New York based news programs—this is due in part to the immense influence New York has on this region's economy and culture, and also to give Connecticut broadcasters the ability to compete with overlapping media coverage from New York-area broadcasters.</p>
<p>NESN broadcasts the <a href="/wiki/Boston_Red_Sox" title="Boston Red Sox">Boston Red Sox</a> baseball and <a href="/wiki/Boston_Bruins" title="Boston Bruins">Boston Bruins</a> hockey throughout the region, save for Fairfield County, Connecticut.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-136"><a href="#cite_note-136">[135]</a></sup> Most of Connecticut, save for Windham county in the state's northeast corner, and even southern Rhode Island, receives the <a href="/wiki/YES_Network" title="YES Network">YES Network</a>, which broadcasts the games of the <a href="/wiki/New_York_Yankees" title="New York Yankees">New York Yankees</a>. For the most part, the same areas also carry <a href="/wiki/SportsNet_New_York" title="SportsNet New York">SportsNet New York</a> (SNY), which broadcasts <a href="/wiki/New_York_Mets" title="New York Mets">New York Mets</a> games.</p>
<p><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Comcast_SportsNet_New_England" title="Comcast SportsNet New England">Comcast SportsNet New England</a> broadcasts the games of the <a href="/wiki/Boston_Celtics" title="Boston Celtics">Boston Celtics</a>, <a href="/wiki/New_England_Revolution" title="New England Revolution">New England Revolution</a> and <a href="/wiki/Boston_Cannons" title="Boston Cannons">Boston Cannons</a>.</p>
<p>While most New England cities have daily newspapers, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Boston_Globe" title="The Boston Globe">The Boston Globe</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/The_New_York_Times" title="The New York Times">The New York Times</a></i> are distributed widely throughout the region. Major newspapers also include <i><a href="/wiki/The_Providence_Journal" title="The Providence Journal">The Providence Journal</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Portland_Press_Herald" title="Portland Press Herald">Portland Press Herald</a></i>, and <i><a href="/wiki/Hartford_Courant" title="Hartford Courant">Hartford Courant</a></i>, the oldest continuously published newspaper in the U.S.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-137"><a href="#cite_note-137">[136]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Comedy">Comedy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=New_England&amp;action=edit&amp;section=45" title="Edit section: Comedy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>New Englanders are well represented in American comedy. Writers for <i><a href="/wiki/The_Simpsons" title="The Simpsons">The Simpsons</a></i> and late-night television programs often come by way of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Harvard_Lampoon" title="Harvard Lampoon">Harvard Lampoon</a>. <i><a href="/wiki/Family_Guy" title="Family Guy">Family Guy</a></i> is an animated sitcom situated in Rhode Island, created by <a href="/wiki/Connecticut" title="Connecticut">Connecticut</a> native and <a href="/wiki/Rhode_Island_School_of_Design" title="Rhode Island School of Design">Rhode Island School of Design</a> graduate <a href="/wiki/Seth_MacFarlane" title="Seth MacFarlane">Seth MacFarlane</a> (along with <i><a href="/wiki/American_Dad!" title="American Dad!">American Dad!</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/The_Cleveland_Show" title="The Cleveland Show">The Cleveland Show</a></i>). A number of <i><a href="/wiki/Saturday_Night_Live" title="Saturday Night Live">Saturday Night Live</a></i> (SNL) cast members have roots in New England, from <a href="/wiki/Adam_Sandler" title="Adam Sandler">Adam Sandler</a> to <a href="/wiki/Amy_Poehler" title="Amy Poehler">Amy Poehler</a>, who also stars in the <a href="/wiki/NBC" title="NBC">NBC</a> television series <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Parks_and_Recreation_(TV_series)" title="Parks and Recreation (TV series)">Parks and Recreation</a></i>. Former <i><a href="/wiki/The_Daily_Show" title="The Daily Show">Daily Show</a></i> correspondents <a href="/wiki/Rob_Corddry" title="Rob Corddry">Rob Corddry</a> and <a href="/wiki/Steve_Carell" title="Steve Carell">Steve Carell</a> are from Massachusetts. Carell was also involved in film and <a href="/wiki/The_Office_(U.S._TV_series)" title="The Office (U.S. TV series)">the American adaptation</a> of <i>The Office</i>, which features <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dunder-Mifflin" title="Dunder-Mifflin">Dunder-Mifflin</a> branches set in <a href="/wiki/Stamford,_Connecticut" title="Stamford, Connecticut">Stamford, Connecticut</a> and <a href="/wiki/Nashua,_New_Hampshire" title="Nashua, New Hampshire">Nashua, New Hampshire</a>.</p>
<p>Late-night television hosts <a href="/wiki/Jay_Leno" title="Jay Leno">Jay Leno</a> and <a href="/wiki/Conan_O%27Brien" title="Conan O'Brien">Conan O'Brien</a> have roots in the Boston area. Notable stand-up comedians are also from the region, including <a href="/wiki/Bill_Burr" title="Bill Burr">Bill Burr</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dane_Cook" title="Dane Cook">Dane Cook</a>, <a href="/wiki/Steve_Sweeney" title="Steve Sweeney">Steve Sweeney</a>, <a href="/wiki/Steven_Wright" title="Steven Wright">Steven Wright</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sarah_Silverman" title="Sarah Silverman">Sarah Silverman</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lisa_Lampanelli" title="Lisa Lampanelli">Lisa Lampanelli</a>, <a href="/wiki/Denis_Leary" title="Denis Leary">Denis Leary</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lenny_Clarke" title="Lenny Clarke">Lenny Clarke</a>, <a href="/wiki/Patrice_O%27Neal" title="Patrice O'Neal">Patrice O'Neal</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Louis_CK" title="Louis CK">Louis CK</a>. <i>SNL</i> cast member <a href="/wiki/Seth_Meyers" title="Seth Meyers">Seth Meyers</a> once attributed the region's imprint on American humor to its "sort of wry New England sense of pointing out anyone who's trying to make a big deal of himself", with the <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Boston_Globe" title="Boston Globe">Boston Globe</a></i> suggesting that <a href="/wiki/Irony" title="Irony">irony</a> and sarcasm are its trademarks, as well as Irish influences.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-138"><a href="#cite_note-138">[137]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Literature">Literature</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=New_England&amp;action=edit&amp;section=46" title="Edit section: Literature">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Literature_of_New_England" title="Literature of New England">Literature of New England</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:RWEmerson.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="359" data-file-width="239" height="330" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b1/RWEmerson.jpg/220px-RWEmerson.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/b/b1/RWEmerson.jpg 1.5x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:RWEmerson.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Ralph_Waldo_Emerson" title="Ralph Waldo Emerson">Ralph Waldo Emerson</a> was born in Boston and spent most of his literary career in <a href="/wiki/Concord,_Massachusetts" title="Concord, Massachusetts">Concord, Massachusetts</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The literature of New England has had an enduring influence on <a href="/wiki/American_literature" title="American literature">American literature</a> in general, with themes that are emblematic of the larger concerns of American letters, such as religion, race, the individual versus society, social repression, and nature.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-139"><a href="#cite_note-139">[138]</a></sup> Famous New England writers include <a href="/wiki/Transcendentalism" title="Transcendentalism">Transcendentalist</a> philosophers <a href="/wiki/Ralph_Waldo_Emerson" title="Ralph Waldo Emerson">Ralph Waldo Emerson</a> and <a href="/wiki/Henry_David_Thoreau" title="Henry David Thoreau">Henry David Thoreau</a>, poets <a href="/wiki/Emily_Dickinson" title="Emily Dickinson">Emily Dickinson</a> and <a href="/wiki/Elizabeth_Bishop" title="Elizabeth Bishop">Elizabeth Bishop</a>, and novelists <a href="/wiki/Nathaniel_Hawthorne" title="Nathaniel Hawthorne">Nathaniel Hawthorne</a> and <a href="/wiki/Harriet_Beecher_Stowe" title="Harriet Beecher Stowe">Harriet Beecher Stowe</a>.</p>
<p>Boston was the center of the American publishing industry for some years, largely on the strength of its local writers and before it was overtaken by New York in the middle of the nineteenth century. Boston remains the home of publishers <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Houghton_Mifflin" title="Houghton Mifflin">Houghton Mifflin</a> and <a href="/wiki/Pearson_Education" title="Pearson Education">Pearson Education</a>, and it was the longtime home of literary magazine <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_Atlantic_Monthly" title="The Atlantic Monthly">The Atlantic Monthly</a></i>. <a href="/wiki/Merriam-Webster" title="Merriam-Webster">Merriam-Webster</a> is based in <a href="/wiki/Springfield,_Massachusetts" title="Springfield, Massachusetts">Springfield, Massachusetts</a>. <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Yankee_Magazine" title="Yankee Magazine">Yankee</a></i> is a magazine for New Englanders based in <a href="/wiki/Dublin,_New_Hampshire" title="Dublin, New Hampshire">Dublin, New Hampshire</a>.</p>
<p>Twentieth and twenty-first century writers hailing from New England include Maine native <a href="/wiki/Stephen_King" title="Stephen King">Stephen King</a> and New Hampshire native <a href="/wiki/John_Irving" title="John Irving">John Irving</a>, and New England is a major setting of their works. <a href="/wiki/George_V._Higgins" title="George V. Higgins">George V. Higgins</a> wrote about life in the New England criminal underworld, while <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/H.P._Lovecraft" title="H.P. Lovecraft">H.P. Lovecraft</a> set many of his works of horror in his native <a href="/wiki/Rhode_Island" title="Rhode Island">Rhode Island</a>.</p>
<h3><span id="Film,_television,_and_acting"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Film.2C_television.2C_and_acting">Film, television, and acting</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=New_England&amp;action=edit&amp;section=47" title="Edit section: Film, television, and acting">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>New England has a rich history in <a href="/wiki/Filmmaking" title="Filmmaking">filmmaking</a> dating back to the dawn of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Motion_picture" title="Motion picture">motion picture</a> era at the turn of the 20th century, sometimes dubbed <a href="/wiki/Hollywood_East" title="Hollywood East">Hollywood East</a> by film critics. A theater at 547 Washington Street in Boston was the second location to debut a picture projected by the <a href="/wiki/Vitascope" title="Vitascope">Vitascope</a>, and shortly thereafter several novels were being adapted for the screen and set in New England, including <i><a href="/wiki/The_Scarlet_Letter" title="The Scarlet Letter">The Scarlet Letter</a></i> and <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_House_of_Seven_Gables" title="The House of Seven Gables">The House of Seven Gables</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-140"><a href="#cite_note-140">[139]</a></sup> The New England region continued to churn out films at a pace above the national average for the duration of the 20th century, including blockbuster hits such as <a href="/wiki/Jaws_(film)" title="Jaws (film)"><i>Jaws</i></a>, <i><a href="/wiki/Good_Will_Hunting" title="Good Will Hunting">Good Will Hunting</a></i>, and <i><a href="/wiki/The_Departed" title="The Departed">The Departed</a></i>, all of which won <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Oscars" title="Oscars">Oscars</a>. The New England area became known for a number of themes that recurred in films made during this era, including the development of yankee characters, smalltown life contrasted with city values, seafaring tales, family secrets, and haunted New England.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-141"><a href="#cite_note-141">[140]</a></sup> These themes are rooted in centuries of New England culture and are complemented by the region's diverse natural landscape and architecture, from the <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Ocean" title="Atlantic Ocean">Atlantic Ocean</a> and brilliant fall foliage to church steeples and skyscrapers.</p>
<p>Since the turn of the millennium, Boston and the greater New England region have been home to the production of numerous films and television series, thanks in part to tax incentive programs put in place by local governments to attract filmmakers to the region.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-142"><a href="#cite_note-142">[141]</a></sup></p>
<p>Notable actors and actresses that have come from the New England area include <a href="/wiki/Ben_Affleck" title="Ben Affleck">Ben Affleck</a>, <a href="/wiki/Matt_Damon" title="Matt Damon">Matt Damon</a>, <a href="/wiki/Amy_Poehler" title="Amy Poehler">Amy Poehler</a>, <a href="/wiki/Elizabeth_Banks" title="Elizabeth Banks">Elizabeth Banks</a>, <a href="/wiki/Steve_Carell" title="Steve Carell">Steve Carell</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ruth_Gordon" title="Ruth Gordon">Ruth Gordon</a>, <a href="/wiki/John_Krasinski" title="John Krasinski">John Krasinski</a>, <a href="/wiki/Edward_Norton" title="Edward Norton">Edward Norton</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mark_Wahlberg" title="Mark Wahlberg">Mark Wahlberg</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Matthew_Perry" title="Matthew Perry">Matthew Perry</a>. A full list of those from Massachusetts can be <a href="/wiki/List_of_people_from_Massachusetts" title="List of people from Massachusetts">found here</a>, and a listing of notable films and television series produced in the area <a href="/wiki/List_of_films_set_in_New_England" title="List of films set in New England">here</a>.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Sports">Sports</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=New_England&amp;action=edit&amp;section=48" title="Edit section: Sports">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Sports_in_New_England" title="Sports in New England">Sports in New England</a></div>
<p>Two popular American sports were invented in New England: <a href="/wiki/Basketball" title="Basketball">basketball</a>, invented by <a href="/wiki/James_Naismith" title="James Naismith">James Naismith</a> (a Canadian) in <a href="/wiki/Springfield,_Massachusetts" title="Springfield, Massachusetts">Springfield, Massachusetts</a>, in 1891,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-143"><a href="#cite_note-143">[142]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Volleyball" title="Volleyball">volleyball</a>, invented in 1895 by <a href="/wiki/William_G._Morgan" title="William G. Morgan">William G. Morgan</a>, in <a href="/wiki/Holyoke,_Massachusetts" title="Holyoke, Massachusetts">Holyoke, Massachusetts</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-144"><a href="#cite_note-144">[143]</a></sup> Additionally, <a href="/wiki/Walter_Camp" title="Walter Camp">Walter Camp</a> is credited with developing modern <a href="/wiki/American_football" title="American football">American football</a> in <a href="/wiki/New_Haven,_Connecticut" title="New Haven, Connecticut">New Haven, Connecticut</a>, in the 1870s and 1880s.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-145"><a href="#cite_note-145">[144]</a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/New_Hampshire_Motor_Speedway" title="New Hampshire Motor Speedway">New Hampshire Motor Speedway</a> is an oval racetrack that has hosted several <a href="/wiki/NASCAR" title="NASCAR">NASCAR</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/American_Championship_Car_Racing" title="American Championship Car Racing">American Championship Car Racing</a> races, whereas <a href="/wiki/Lime_Rock_Park" title="Lime Rock Park">Lime Rock Park</a> in Connecticut is a traditional <a href="/wiki/Road_racing" title="Road racing">road racing</a> venue home of <a href="/wiki/Sports_car_racing" title="Sports car racing">sports car races</a>. Events at these venues have had the "New England" moniker, such as the <a href="/wiki/NASCAR" title="NASCAR">NASCAR</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/New_England_300" title="New England 300">New England 300</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/CNBC_Prime%27s_%22The_Profit%22_200" title="CNBC Prime's &quot;The Profit&quot; 200">New England 200</a>, the <a href="/wiki/IndyCar_Series" title="IndyCar Series">IndyCar Series</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/New_England_Indy_200" title="New England Indy 200">New England Indy 200</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/American_Le_Mans_Series" title="American Le Mans Series">American Le Mans Series</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/New_England_Grand_Prix" title="New England Grand Prix">New England Grand Prix</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Professional_and_semi-professional_sports_teams">Professional and semi-professional sports teams</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=New_England&amp;action=edit&amp;section=49" title="Edit section: Professional and semi-professional sports teams">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Fenway_Park.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="704" data-file-width="1648" height="94" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/Fenway_Park.jpg/220px-Fenway_Park.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/Fenway_Park.jpg/330px-Fenway_Park.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/Fenway_Park.jpg/440px-Fenway_Park.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Fenway_Park.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Fenway_Park" title="Fenway Park">Fenway Park</a>, home of the <a href="/wiki/Boston_Red_Sox" title="Boston Red Sox">Boston Red Sox</a>, is the oldest operating ballpark in the U.S.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The major professional sports teams in New England are based in Massachusetts: the <a href="/wiki/Boston_Red_Sox" title="Boston Red Sox">Boston Red Sox</a>, the <a href="/wiki/New_England_Patriots" title="New England Patriots">New England Patriots</a> (based in <a href="/wiki/Foxborough,_Massachusetts" title="Foxborough, Massachusetts">Foxborough, Massachusetts</a>), the <a href="/wiki/Boston_Celtics" title="Boston Celtics">Boston Celtics</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Boston_Bruins" title="Boston Bruins">Boston Bruins</a>, the <a href="/wiki/New_England_Revolution" title="New England Revolution">New England Revolution</a> (also based in Foxborough), the <a href="/wiki/Boston_Breakers" title="Boston Breakers">Boston Breakers</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Boston_Cannons" title="Boston Cannons">Boston Cannons</a>. Hartford had a professional hockey team, the <a href="/wiki/Hartford_Whalers" title="Hartford Whalers">Hartford Whalers</a>, from 1975 until they moved to <a href="/wiki/North_Carolina" title="North Carolina">North Carolina</a> in 1997. A <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/WNBA" title="WNBA">WNBA</a> team, the <a href="/wiki/Connecticut_Sun" title="Connecticut Sun">Connecticut Sun</a>, are based in southeastern Connecticut at the <a href="/wiki/Mohegan_Sun" title="Mohegan Sun">Mohegan Sun</a> resort, which is also home to the professional indoor lacrosse team the <a href="/wiki/New_England_Black_Wolves" title="New England Black Wolves">New England Black Wolves</a>. New England is also home to the <a href="/wiki/Boston_Blades" title="Boston Blades">Boston Blades</a>, <a href="/wiki/Boston_Pride" title="Boston Pride">Boston Pride</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Connecticut_Whale_(NWHL)" title="Connecticut Whale (NWHL)">Connecticut Whale</a>, which represent three of the five professional women's hockey teams in the United States.</p>
<p>There are also minor league baseball and hockey teams based in larger cities such as the <a href="/wiki/Bridgeport_Bluefish" title="Bridgeport Bluefish">Bridgeport Bluefish</a> (baseball), the <a href="/wiki/Bridgeport_Sound_Tigers" title="Bridgeport Sound Tigers">Bridgeport Sound Tigers</a> (hockey), the <a href="/wiki/Connecticut_Tigers" title="Connecticut Tigers">Connecticut Tigers</a> (baseball), the <a href="/wiki/Hartford_Yard_Goats" title="Hartford Yard Goats">Hartford Yard Goats</a> (baseball), the <a href="/wiki/Hartford_Wolf_Pack" title="Hartford Wolf Pack">Hartford Wolf Pack</a> (hockey), the <a href="/wiki/Lowell_Spinners" title="Lowell Spinners">Lowell Spinners</a> (baseball), the <a href="/wiki/Manchester_Monarchs_(ECHL)" title="Manchester Monarchs (ECHL)">Manchester Monarchs</a> (hockey), the <a href="/wiki/New_Britain_Bees" title="New Britain Bees">New Britain Bees</a> (baseball), the <a href="/wiki/New_Hampshire_Fisher_Cats" title="New Hampshire Fisher Cats">New Hampshire Fisher Cats</a> (baseball), the <a href="/wiki/Pawtucket_Red_Sox" title="Pawtucket Red Sox">Pawtucket Red Sox</a> (baseball), the <a href="/wiki/Portland_Sea_Dogs" title="Portland Sea Dogs">Portland Sea Dogs</a> (baseball), the <a href="/wiki/Providence_Bruins" title="Providence Bruins">Providence Bruins</a> (hockey), the <a href="/wiki/Springfield_Thunderbirds" title="Springfield Thunderbirds">Springfield Thunderbirds</a> (hockey), the <a href="/wiki/Vermont_Lake_Monsters" title="Vermont Lake Monsters">Vermont Lake Monsters</a> (baseball), and the <a href="/wiki/Worcester_Railers" title="Worcester Railers">Worcester Railers</a> (hockey).</p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/NBA_G_League" title="NBA G League">NBA G League</a> fields a team in New England: the <a href="/wiki/Maine_Red_Claws" title="Maine Red Claws">Maine Red Claws</a>, based in <a href="/wiki/Portland,_Maine" title="Portland, Maine">Portland, Maine</a>. The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Springfield_Armor" title="Springfield Armor">Springfield Armor</a> in <a href="/wiki/Springfield,_Massachusetts" title="Springfield, Massachusetts">Springfield, Massachusetts</a>, previously played in the region. The Red Claws are affiliated with the <a href="/wiki/Boston_Celtics" title="Boston Celtics">Boston Celtics</a> and the Armor were affiliated with the <a href="/wiki/Brooklyn_Nets" title="Brooklyn Nets">Brooklyn Nets</a>, prior to relocating to <a href="/wiki/Grand_Rapids,_Michigan" title="Grand Rapids, Michigan">Grand Rapids, Michigan</a>, to become the <a href="/wiki/Grand_Rapids_Drive" title="Grand Rapids Drive">Grand Rapids Drive</a>. New England is also represented in the <a href="/wiki/Premier_Basketball_League" title="Premier Basketball League">Premier Basketball League</a> by the <a href="/wiki/Vermont_Frost_Heaves" title="Vermont Frost Heaves">Vermont Frost Heaves</a> of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Barre,_Vermont_(city)" title="Barre, Vermont (city)">Barre, Vermont</a>.</p>
<p>Thanksgiving Day high school football rivalries date back to the 19th century, and the Harvard-Yale rivalry ("<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Harvard-Yale_football_games_(The_Game)" title="Harvard-Yale football games (The Game)">The Game</a>") is the oldest active rivalry in college football. The <a href="/wiki/Boston_Marathon" title="Boston Marathon">Boston Marathon</a>, run on <a href="/wiki/Patriots%27_Day" title="Patriots' Day">Patriots' Day</a> every year, is a New England cultural institution and the oldest annual marathon in the world. While the race offers far less prize money than many other marathons, the race's difficulty and long history make it one of the world's most prestigious marathons.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-146"><a href="#cite_note-146">[145]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Transportation">Transportation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=New_England&amp;action=edit&amp;section=50" title="Edit section: Transportation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Transportation_in_New_England" title="Transportation in New England">Transportation in New England</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:MBTA_Commuter_Rail_and_funding_district_map.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="553" data-file-width="904" height="184" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/MBTA_Commuter_Rail_and_funding_district_map.svg/300px-MBTA_Commuter_Rail_and_funding_district_map.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/MBTA_Commuter_Rail_and_funding_district_map.svg/450px-MBTA_Commuter_Rail_and_funding_district_map.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/MBTA_Commuter_Rail_and_funding_district_map.svg/600px-MBTA_Commuter_Rail_and_funding_district_map.svg.png 2x" width="300"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:MBTA_Commuter_Rail_and_funding_district_map.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The <a href="/wiki/MBTA_Commuter_Rail" title="MBTA Commuter Rail">MBTA Commuter Rail</a> serves much of Massachusetts and parts of Rhode Island radiating from Downtown Boston, with plans for expansion into New Hampshire.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-147"><a href="#cite_note-147">[146]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-148"><a href="#cite_note-148">[147]</a></sup></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Massachusetts_Bay_Transportation_Authority" title="Massachusetts Bay Transportation Authority">Massachusetts Bay Transportation Authority</a> (MBTA) provides rail and <a href="/wiki/Rapid_transit" title="Rapid transit">subway</a> service within the Boston metropolitan area, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bus_service" title="Bus service">bus service</a> in Greater Boston, and <a href="/wiki/Commuter_rail" title="Commuter rail">commuter rail</a> service throughout Eastern Massachusetts and parts of Rhode Island. The New York City <a href="/wiki/Metropolitan_Transportation_Authority" title="Metropolitan Transportation Authority">Metropolitan Transportation Authority</a> in partnership with the <a href="/wiki/Connecticut_Department_of_Transportation" title="Connecticut Department of Transportation">Connecticut Department of Transportation</a> (CTDOT) operates the <a href="/wiki/Metro-North_Railroad" title="Metro-North Railroad">Metro-North Railroad</a>, which provides commuter rail service in Southwestern Connecticut in the corridor between New York City and <a href="/wiki/New_Haven,_Connecticut" title="New Haven, Connecticut">New Haven</a>. CTDOT provides the <a href="/wiki/Shore_Line_East" title="Shore Line East">Shore Line East</a> commuter rail service along the Connecticut coastline east of New Haven, terminating in <a href="/wiki/Old_Saybrook,_Connecticut" title="Old Saybrook, Connecticut">Old Saybrook</a> and <a href="/wiki/New_London,_Connecticut" title="New London, Connecticut">New London</a>.</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Amtrak" title="Amtrak">Amtrak</a> provides interstate rail service throughout New England. Boston is the northern terminus of the <a href="/wiki/Northeast_Corridor" title="Northeast Corridor">Northeast Corridor</a>. The <i><a href="/wiki/Vermonter_(train)" title="Vermonter (train)">Vermonter</a></i> connects Vermont to Massachusetts and Connecticut, while the <i><a href="/wiki/Downeaster_(train)" title="Downeaster (train)">Downeaster</a></i> links Maine to Boston. The long-distance <i><a href="/wiki/Lake_Shore_Limited" title="Lake Shore Limited">Lake Shore Limited</a></i> train has two eastern termini after splitting in <a href="/wiki/Albany,_New_York" title="Albany, New York">Albany</a>, one of which is Boston. This provides rail service on the former <a href="/wiki/Boston_and_Albany_Railroad" title="Boston and Albany Railroad">Boston and Albany Railroad</a>, which runs between its namesake cities. The rest of the <i>Lake Shore Limited</i> continues to New York City.</p>
